Eight

by Alexis_Payton

Summary

Now, as a bona fide member of an eclectic coven, Agatha could admit that she hadn’t always been the most reasonable witch. Having actual friends has made her more inclined to reflect and grow. And as a result of this newfound propensity toward introspection, she could recognise that there was something gravely wrong with her. Because even when her life finally felt liveable again, a pervasive want continued to eat away at her soul and sanity.
Naturally, it was then, whilst drowning in uncertainty and poorly dealing with a best friend hinting at wanting to be more, that Agatha’s volatile past quite literally comes crashing into her carefully reconstructed life.

Notes

The "minor Wagatha FWB" tag is reflective of what's planned for this fic. I won't be adding them as a pairing tag as that would create an expectation that won't be met. This is an Agathario fic that also focuses on Agatha and her relationship with her coven.

Chapter 1: The Blood Moon

The Blood Moon was considered a potent time for transformation and banishing negativity. As a default, Agatha Harkness was a transformation hobbyist and a connoisseur of negativity. Embodying it, verbalising it, basking in it. So it remained a constant surprise, how after four years of lunar cycles spent in the woods around a campfire with her coven, she couldn’t muster an ounce of that cynicism she’d relished in for over three hundred years. Especially not when they’d just completed a Hexenbesen flight over Westview, circling all the way out to Eastview and back. And not when Alice had finally mastered her shielding spells, which allowed them to remain undetected in the clear night sky.

Agatha practically glowed with pride, the banishment of negativity a resounding success. The early summer evening was pleasantly warm, the sound of Alice lightly picking at her guitar strings while Jen, Lilia, and Billy softly spoke amongst themselves, brought Agatha nothing but peace and contentment.

Or maybe it was the lovingly cultivated indica strain she’d smoked earlier that made her feel weightless in her comfy camping chair cloud.

Maybe it was Wanda seated beside her, bloodshot eyes droopily staring into the fire, her gorgeous red hair illuminated by the flames. Or, more likely, it was Wanda’s intoxicating magic that buzzed hypnotically beneath her skin, making all the hair on Agatha’s body stand on end.

Drawing in a sharp breath through her nose, she shot up from her seat, needing to move. The guitar and conversation halted and her coven looked to her, amused and unsurprised.

“I’m going home,” Agatha announced, unnecessarily imperious, ignoring their fond smiles that turned to smirks when Wanda stood as well.

“Come see me tomorrow,” Lilia said, causing everyone to briefly tense up.

Agatha narrowed her eyes but didn’t want to deal with whatever that was about right then. So she nodded and waved a dismissive hand in their general direction. “Don’t get too drunk, I’m not bailing anyone out of jail tonight.”

They were already illegally building fires in the woods. Nothing a little spell or two couldn’t get them out of. But they would need either Wanda or Agatha to smoothly get that done.

“Good night you two,” Jen’s teasing voice called after them.

“’Night, coven,” Wanda called over her shoulder and fell into step beside Agatha, like a magnet.

A few minutes into their silent and leisurely stroll through the woods, and Agatha’s high had settled into a pleasing hum.

Wanda linked their arms. “Jen and Alice are still having sex,” she said, accent thick and pleasantly curling around her tongue. Pretty green eyes now clear and glittering in the moonlight.

“I’m not sure why they’re trying to hide it,” Agatha mumbled, feeling heat rise at the back of her neck.

“It’s difficult transitioning a friendship into a relationship when your worried that you might lose your best friend if things go wrong...”

Agatha hummed, ignoring Wanda’s knowing gaze on her face, and the soothing squeeze on her bicep.

“I'm thinking of quitting the library job.” Wanda thankfully changed course away from that hazardous discussion.

“Yeah? Wanna bum it at home with me?”

“Maybe, for a little while. I need to try something new again.”

Agatha frowned when she sounded ashamed at the admittance. “Nothing wrong with trying out different things until you find what you like.”

“Yeah.”

“Are you feeling antsy?”

“A little.”

“Maybe our vacation will help with that.”

“Possibly.”

Agatha stopped and looked at her, lifting a brow.

Wanda shrugged. “I’m feeling stuck. Indecisive.” She got them walking again, pulling Agatha along.

“Don't force it, hotstuff. There's no rush.”

“I feel like I’m wasting my life. Letting people down. Like I should be doing something more with all this power.”

Wanda had once cast a hex on the entire town. A hex so complex and effortlessly masterful, it had Agatha salivating to meet her. Their fight had been spectacular. A fight Wanda had won because Agatha still hadn’t learned when to keep her mouth shut. Rather, she hadn’t quite learned when to not show off when in the presence of a beautiful and powerful woman.

They’d known each other five years. The first three had predominantly consisted of them dealing with their grief and anger. Their regrets and mistakes. The plan had been to make Wanda believe that Agatha was a friend, make her feel indebted, and then try to take her power again when she least expected it. Instead, Agatha had gone and forged a friendship she was actually invested in sustaining.

How humiliating.

“You don’t owe anyone anything, hon,” she said. “You've had people telling you what they want you to do for them for most of your life. Fuck’em, I say.” Agatha smirked and took Wanda’s hand, leading her out of the woods and onto the sidewalk down their street.

Westview at night was quiet, even on a Friday. They were the only two people walking through the suburban neighbourhood with its neatly trimmed lawns and far too many white picket fences. In town centre, the bell tower heralded in twelve o’clock. Agatha was irrationally irritated that it was electronic. That the tolls indicating noon and midnight came from a speaker, despite the giant brass bell that hung there, aesthetically pleasing yet functionally redundant.

“Maybe it’s this place,” Agatha murmured, despite knowing that it was just Wanda.

Wanda was far too kind. Too forgiving, and had offered Agatha a chance at making amends through teaching her about magic and how to control her chaos. Agatha had to convince her to let the people of Westview forget that they’d been held captive and mentally tortured for the duration of Wanda’s grandiose breakdown.

They knew each other inside and out. All the bad parts and insecurities. Which was why Agatha suspected that hand-waving away what the hex had done, still had Wanda simmering in guilt and feeling like she hadn’t really taken accountability. Personally, Agatha thought the people of Westview were better off not remembering at all.

The combination of Wanda’s hex and Agatha’s mind control had fried the brain of the guy whose house she’d appropriated. When Wanda’s spell lifted and Agatha was defeated, he’d taken off like a lunatic before Agatha could fix him up like she usually did all her marks. Too preoccupied dealing with a volatile Scarlet Witch who’d just lost her Vision for a second—third?—time, so she really had more pressing matters to attend to than chasing him down.

Regardless, mind control didn’t need to lead to brain damage and PTSD was what Agatha struggled to convince Wanda of. It was still grossly invasive and Agatha would kill anyone who tried it on her, so she could understand Wanda’s guilt, but it was really for the best to not leave behind any loose ends.

“We could move,” Agatha offered. An antsy Scarlet Witch was not something anyone wanted to deal with.

“You love it here.”

Agatha huffed. “Love is a strong word. It’s convenient here.”

Westview was small and remote. Agatha could control perceptions without interfering too much in town life. It was a safe and secure place for the coven to thrive in.

“Well, I love it here,” Wanda said with a put on pout she knew would have Agatha rolling her eyes, then broke into a grin when she did. “Maybe I could become a shady criminal like you.”

Agatha chuckled. “You're too nice to be the type of criminal I am.”

“I'm not that nice.”

“That was more a testament to my level of criminality rather than your capability. You can be my arch nemesis. I'll start robbing banks again and we can have tension filled encounters after each heist.”

“What does it pay?” Wanda asked, a dangerous smile curling around her lips as they strolled up the pathway to the large three bedroom house they shared.

“Depends,” Agatha said, opening the front door and holding it for her.

Wanda brushed up against her like a cat, stopping close and stared into Agatha’s eyes. “Depends on what?” she whispered.

“On what you’re wearing when you come to foil my plans.” Agatha smirked and followed Wanda’s husky laughter into the house.

 

They retreated to their respective rooms, Agatha showering away the remainder of her high. She pulled on a pair of light cotton pyjama shorts and a tank top, the evening too warm for anything else. Exiting the house again into the backyard, she entered her massive greenhouse.

Pruning always cleared her head. There was something therapeutic about cutting away the deadness, blight, and imperfections. It was always in-season in her garden. Various spells controlled the temperature and light, but Agatha irrigated by hand, preferring to judge for herself how much water each plant required. She also worked the soil and made her own mulch, compost, and bone meal.

Cliche as it might be, she enjoyed tending roses the most. The largest section of the greenhouse was covered in them, with a few herbs and cannabis plants partitioned at the back, not allowed to share the same air as her precious babies.

Agatha’s roses were the envy in town. Everyone kept asking her for arrangements as though she was a fucking florist. Bluntly telling them no and watching the surprise on their faces was deliciously entertaining. She didn’t let anyone in her greenhouse anymore. Wanda was banned permanently after she invited Mrs. Hart over, who then decided to not shut up about what she had seen. She’d taken pictures and told the town paper and Agatha had been harassed for two years to please exhibit her roses at the bi-annual town fair, until she was forced to magic that nuisance away.

Craving something sweet after she finished checking on things—stood there for a few minutes basking in the scent that always soothed her—she headed to the kitchen and got out a container of seedless red grapes. Sitting at the kitchen island, she popped them into her mouth one by one and thought over her and Wanda’s earlier conversation.

She’d been a nomad before Westview, before Wanda and the coven. They could probably travel more, but Wanda was still very recognisable even after years off the grid. When she’d reset the citizens of Westview’s minds, Agatha had slightly changed their recollection of Wanda the Avenger’s physical appearance. Granted, Wanda wasn’t as prominent and ostentatious as Iron Man or Captain America had been at the time, but still pretty unforgettable.

Maybe she could work on a shapeshifting spell. Those could really mess with a person mentally when they were used for too long, so she hadn’t suggested it yet.

Making little notes on her phone, she continued to muse over the pros and cons of glamour versus shapeshifting spells, until Wanda entered the kitchen in a sinful scarlet teddy and Agatha nearly choked on a grape. She watched Wanda’s long legs when she lifted onto her toes, the silky material shifting high on her thighs, to remove a glass from the cupboard, before making her way to the sink and filling it with water.

Wanda then casually turned around to face her, leaning back against the sink, showing off a set of hard nipples as she slowly drank from her glass and stared at Agatha with hooded eyes.

They were friends. They’d also been having sex for the duration of that friendship. In the beginning, it had been filled with reckless rage, rough and raw. A hungry, angry exchange of magic and bodily fluids. That was back before they’d destroyed the copy of the Darkhold Agatha had been in possession of. Back when the only way Agatha could think of Wanda was as a source of mouth-watering magic she wanted to consume. Back before the destruction of the Darkhold had left an emptiness inside of her as though she’d had her heart ripped out once again.

She imagined that was how alcoholics felt. Constantly craving and jittery with need. Agatha missed siphoning. Something she could only do when attuned to the Darkhold. Two years since and Agatha wasn’t sure how to be a witch any longer, putting on an air of confidence for her coven to not have them worry.

How could she tell them that the Darkhold still had a hold on her? That she mourned it like a dead lover. Her thoughts, her dreams, often reminisced on the way Wanda’s magic had pulsed through her veins and rumbled in her chest, had shot right between her legs…

Sex and magic. Agatha wasn’t sure how to separate them anymore. She’d wielded both as weapons for centuries. Had to rewire her brain entirely and still she struggled. Every day was a constant struggle.

Chaos magic buzzed wildly beneath Wanda’s skin. Teasing Agatha. Always most inviting during the full moon. Begging Agatha to take it all. To make it her own.

She screwed her eyes shut.

It made her sick to reduce her attraction to simply that. Wanda was attractive, funny, and caring. Agatha would openly admit that she loved her friend. Breathing in the sweet scent of Wanda’s freshly showered skin, Agatha placed a kiss to her shoulder, dragging her focus from the tempting magic to Wanda’s gorgeous body.

After, once they’d caught their breath, Agatha kissed Wanda on the cheek and turned to get up and go to her room. Wanda though, reached out and took her hand, halting her in place. Agatha glanced at her over her shoulder.

“Stay,” Wanda said, gaze earnest and brow furrowed.

Agatha needed to leave. She was struggling to navigate having both friends and a coven. It had been literal centuries since she’d been in a relationship. Well, she’d been in one committed relationship her entire life and she wasn’t quite sure how to be in another.

The vulnerability on Wanda’s face though, had her laying back down and wrapping her arms around Wanda when she shifted to lay with her head on Agatha’s shoulder. Wanda knew her apprehension, her worries and fears. It wasn’t as though Wanda herself knew much about romantic relationships either, only having had one significant clusterfuck under her belt as well.

They understood each other like no one else could. Problem was, Agatha didn’t trust herself to have good things. She only knew how to destroy them. Wanda as a friend was something she was determined to cling to no matter what she had to give up in the process.

She barely slept. Drifting in and out of consciousness, her arms remained firmly around a softly snoring Wanda. Her mind wouldn’t stop. Stray thoughts, insecurities, plans to keep the coven safe and prospering. The cuttings she was cultivating in the greenhouse and the own roots she had to coax from the soil. Spells she needed to teach Alice, and the latest season of Love Island she couldn’t stop hate-watching because heterosexuals were absolutely ridiculous.

She’d been more focused when she’d held the Darkhold. Always a scheme, a plan to gain more power. A direction and a goal she was working toward. Clear and confident in her actions and decisions. Now she was broken. Irreparably, it would appear. Agatha Harkness had been destroyed along with the Book of Sins.

Her eye caught the green ouroboros tattoos around her wrists, a dragon chasing its own tail. It looked similar to the great wyrms of Chinese mythology, long and sleek with thin black climbing rose vines creeping across their bodies. As always, her stomach knotted when she let her thoughts wander too long when looking at them. Under her gaze, they became gorgeously animated, ominously circling her wrists.

 Every magic user she has met could see the dragons, see their circling and the way the roses would bud and bloom. These days, very few seemed to know that they weren’t simply a set of pretty magical tattoos.

Sun rays glinted against the emerald scales and Agatha decided it was an appropriate time to leave. She magically swapped her body with a pillow, but a sleeping Wanda wasn’t fooled,  unhappily grumbling before scrunching the pillow to her chest and sinking back into a deeper sleep.

Smiling fondly, Agatha quietly left the room and got ready to go out. She washed the sex from her body, braided her hair into two pigtails, and put on the cleanest comfiest outfit she could find. Downstairs she switched on the coffee machine and stuck a post-it note onto it, stating she was going to collect brunch from Alice’s.

Donning a hat and her sunglasses she left the house, cringing when she stepped onto the sidewalk and spotted her arch-nemesis fiddling with her mediocre rose bushes. Agatha crossed the street to not have to pass her by.

“Oh! Good morning, Agatha!” Mrs. Hart waved excitedly, rising from her bushes like a demonic entity. Agatha could not stand her. She was too loud, too happy. She gave her a headache during ninety eight per cent of their interactions. Worst of all, every fortnight, Wanda dragged Agatha over to have dinner at the recently widowed woman’s house and now Agatha had been designated a friend by association.

Wanda loved Mrs. Hart. It had started out as a guilty conscience, but the two of them seemed to have genuinely bonded. They were growing subpar weed in Mrs. Hart’s backyard for ‘medicinal’ use and always found a way to involve Agatha in it to probe her for advice and tips. Getting high was the only way she made it through those dinners. Wanda also got very horny after they socialised, so at least there was a bright side.

Maybe that was why she couldn’t settle properly, possibly some inherent fear of losing the person she was entirely were she to just enjoy the good things in her life. Six was also a good number for spiritual balance.

Away from home.

 

Kale Kare was closed. On a Saturday. Jen couldn’t even pretend that she was running a legitimate business. Finally having a one hundred per cent pure organic product range had really taken its toll on her. She had a small international customer base she catered to with a special range of magic potions, only using the organic beauty line as a front.

One would think that Agatha and Wanda had the most to overcome on their road to friendship, but where Agatha had failed in taking Wanda’s magic, she’d inadvertently caused Jen to be bound for over a century. Breaking the binding spell had been only the first step to making amends, forming the coven and offering some power in the world they lived in, had been step two. It took time and exposure therapy, but eventually Jen had thawed enough to where she’d become the person Agatha preferred to spend the most time with when Wanda wasn’t around.

She let herself into the shop and spotted Jen reclining on one of the two facial beds, full face mask on and soft instrumental music playing in the background. Placing her takeout bag, hat, and sunglasses down, Agatha walked to the storage space in the back, through the warded door and into Jen’s alchemy lab, and pulled the hangover elixir from a shelf. The coven was linked from years of ritually channelling magic. Able to reach out and feel each other’s presence and teleport to one another in a pinch over short distances.

Tuning into Alice, Agatha performed an incantation that sent the elixir to the deli, then walked back out to the shop floor. She scanned through Jen’s selection of face masks and grabbed a cucumber, green and oolong tea mask for herself, grateful Jen hadn’t jumped on that gross tallow trend Sarah Proctor wouldn’t shut up about, and took the seat beside her, placing the mask on her face.

 They laid in blissful silence for a long while, and Agatha may have dozed off at one point.

“You want to talk about whatever’s going on between you and Wanda?” Jen eventually murmured.

“After we talk about whatever’s happening between you and Alice.”

“Guess we’ll spend the next few minutes of your spiral in continued silence then.”

“Thanks. Though, do you know why Lilia wants to see me?”

“Probably about our vacation. If she tells you a hurricane’s hitting the Bahamas just pick any location where we can have some sun and beach and book it.”

“Anything to see Alice’s abs in a bikini.”

Jen hummed and Agatha smiled, more of the tension seeping from her body. She refused to go home and make Wanda feel bad because she was unable to act like a normal person.

Though, Jen and Alice shared a house in Eastview, Lilia had moved to Westview and chose the same set up she had before, a small shop in the front and living area in the back.

The properties were all registered in Agatha’s name and she distributed the profits by pushing them back into the coven’s various businesses, investment portfolios and off-shore accounts.

They had a small fortune saved up, in case they needed to go on the run and start over. Agatha still couldn’t believe they entrusted her with their savings knowing exactly who she was. Who she had been? She couldn’t figure it out and they really were a bunch of idiots for having such unequivocal faith in her.

“You wanted to see me?”

She rolled her eyes. “I’ve got stuff to do, Lilia. Just lay it on me. Am I dying?”

Lilia sighed and led her to the kitchen where she put the kettle on. Agatha obediently went to sit at the table. Not saying anything while Lilia made tea. She’d already had a gallon of coffee that day, but accepted the cup anyway.

“I saw darkness.”

“All of ours. The entire coven. Not Billy, though. It felt like we were together, but everything was black.”

Caught up in her head once again, Agatha wished she could’ve said that she had a feeling something bad was about to happen. But it was a pretty normal Saturday in Westview, save for the shadow that fell across the town. The sun appeared to be mid an unscheduled eclipse.

Agatha stood staring up at the sky, impulsively reaching out her magic to check in with the coven. Sensing her distress, she felt them all respond, hurrying out onto the street Agatha had been dragging her feet on all day. It took over three minutes, more than enough time for them to have run, cast a teleportation spell to far away from there. But they stood frozen in place, watching the ball of fire about the size of a small car now, shooting over Westview, clearing town centre, clearing the residential area, and crashing into the field outside of town with a massive boom that had the earth trembling beneath their feet.

Agatha looked to the coven staring at her with wide eyes, but before she could say anything, the sound of a fighter jet following the trajectory of the supposed meteorite, drew her attention. Helicopter blades could be heard approaching in the distance. They would’ve probably been tracking whatever it was for a while, especially if it had come from space.

“Okay,” Agatha said. “The town’s fine. They’ll be focused on whatever that was. Let’s just keep everything clean on our side, yeah?”

They all nodded distractedly, watching the increasing number of military aircraft heading for Westview.

 

Chapter 2: The Meteorite

The coven gathered up in the bell tower, which used to be a watch tower, back in the day when the citizens of Westview had to defend the land they’d stolen from others trying to steal it from them. They were magically shielded from prying eyes, staring out across the tent village that had popped up seemingly within minutes of the meteorite crashing into Westview. The crater had been covered with a massive green canopy and it looked as though the entire military industrial complex had assembled to investigate.

Which could only mean that it might not be a meteorite at all.

Wanda stood rigidly beside her, red irises skidding over the activity in the distance. S.W.O.R.D. was down there too but Wanda’s acquaintance, Captain Monica Rambeau, was somewhere up in space last she'd heard.

Because the government enjoyed a good cover-up, they’d worked with Captain Rambeau to ensure the hex came down in a manner that wouldn’t spook anyone watching from the outside. She could only imagine the number of road vehicle accidents they’d prevented by not letting the air be torn apart out of nowhere.

A crunching sound drew Agatha’s attention to the other three squished together, catching Lilia’s hand withdrawing from the bag of caramel popcorn held to Jen’s chest.

“You guys brought snacks?”

Alice offered her some roasted cashew nuts. Agatha shook a few into her palm and looked back at the spectacle, chewing contemplatively.

“I can get us in there,” Wanda said. “With my magic.”

Agatha gave her a long look. They’d been practising. Messed around with a few people. Nothing intense, just quickly slipping in and out of minds in the most unobtrusive way. Nothing matching the extreme control an infiltration into a remote military base would require, though. Nothing where they were at risk of being classified a national security threat, if caught.

Besides, Agatha’s main concern at present was those agencies stumbling upon Wanda. There would probably be more than a few people who remembered the last time they’d been in Westview. Two anomalous events within five years was highly suspicious. Whatever tale Captain Rambeau had spun to get them to leave them alone would not hold up after something strange happened again in a town that most people didn’t know existed.

Agatha had to get in there and do damage control. To make them forget and ignore the town and the coven while they investigated whatever that thing was.

“We can’t risk them recognising you,” she said.

Wanda’s big doe eyes shifted to her. “I can do it, Agatha.”

Agatha brushed her hair out of her face and breathed out through her nose. “If you’re sure.”

“I’m sure.”

Wanda’s power was linked to her emotions and always would be. Under controlled conditions she did great. Under pressure, well, they haven’t had many opportunities to effectively practise that. If anything went wrong though, Agatha would be there to get them through it. She’d magicked herself out of worse situations before. Back when she had the Darkhold. She was still more powerful than the average witch, just minus a few favoured spells she’d unfortunately made her entire personality.

“I’ll teleport us out at the first sign of trouble,” she reluctantly agreed.

She was curious, though. A little excited. Something was pulling her toward the crater. Like it was calling to her. A strong inviting pulse thrummed in her chest each time she focused her magic toward it.

Wanda grinned, bright and enthusiastic. And maybe they did need to get a bit more adventure in their lives. Wanda seemed to crave the peace and quiet after the life she’d led. But maybe a little chaos on occasion would do them good. Agatha certainly wasn’t built to simply exist in the suburbs.

“All right, ladies,” she said. “Wanda and I will go in tonight when half of them are hopefully sleeping. Try to steer their attention away from town and the coven and hopefully find out what that thing was that fell from the sky.”

“I’m going with you—

“Thank god I don’t need to go in there—

Jen glared at Alice. “You’re not going with them.”

“I can shield us while Wanda does her mindfuckery. It’s less pressure on her and Agatha.”

Alice there would make it a walk in the park, but Agatha was wise enough not to say anything, already confident in what Alice would decide.

Jen and Alice intently stared at each other until Jen sighed. “Fine, Lilia and I will wait nearby in case you three get caught.”

Lilia only raised her eyebrows at being volunteered and continued eating her popcorn, staring thoughtfully toward the response base. Agatha suspected that Lilia didn’t share the majority of her visions with them. Mostly because they were irrelevant, but sometimes it was because Lilia was still trying to parse the information together before dropping a bomb on them.

Regardless, that look in Lilia’s eye told Agatha that whatever went down later that night, it was going to be interesting.

#

Alice and Jen went to fetch Billy who had been left to man the deli and took him home. Wanda decided to go meditate in preparation of their infiltration, and Agatha left with Lilia to help clear away her wall of monitors. None of it was technically illegal, just highly suspicious. Like their bank accounts should anyone care to look at why the coven’s businesses were fairing so well in a town with so few people and a non-existent tourist draw. Kale Kare could explain away a lot with doctored online sales and an excellent investment portfolio, but Lilia and Alice would suffer the most scrutiny under a magnifying glass.

Agatha cast an extra-dimensional space behind Lilia’s study and moved the equipment inside, eyeing the various trunks Lilia rolled toward her to stow away as well.

“Are these dead bodies?”

“Do you not want plausible deniability?”

“Just asking if I need to change the temperature in here or not.”

“Sixty-eight to seventy-seven degrees should be ideal for everything.”

“Yes, ma’am,” Agatha muttered and did as she was told.

When she was finally done hiding away Lilia’s secrets, she flicked her hair away from her face and looked around the apartment. “You’re going to need to use your laptop. I know it’s difficult to see the tiny numbers in your old age, but we’ll be fine if you miss a selling or buying opportunity or two, or whatever it is you do to make us rich.”

“Hm. We’ll be getting even richer next week. Don’t you worry your pretty little head about that.”

Agatha grinned. “Aw, you think I’m pretty, Lilia?”

“Only when you don’t speak,” she drawled.

Agatha chuckled. “Why don’t you come and stay with Wanda and I for a while, until this mess blows over?”

“I’d rather not be around all that tension.”

“What tension?” Agatha asked, affronted that Lilia would dare mention her business when Agatha had just spent half an hour not questioning a single one of her mysterious trunks and chests.

Lilia raised a brow. “Are we talking about this?”

“No.”

She took hold of Agatha’s wrist staring pointedly at the green ouroboros tattoo. “How about we talk about this and how it’s possibly related to that which we aren’t talking about?”

“But I don’t want to.”

“Wanda’s a good girl,” Lilia softly said.

Agatha stiffened, resisting the urge to rip her hand from Lilia’s grasp.

“Have you told her the truth about these?”

“She knows I was married. That we’re estranged. That’s what these mean and it doesn’t matter.”

“Agatha—

“It doesn’t matter.”

“Hand-fasting tattoos of estranged spouses fade. They fade the second one of them wants out. These are as bright as ever. They seem brighter than the day I met you. She’s going to find out.”

Agatha finally wrenched her wrist free and placed both hands under her armpits, hiding the tattoos away and hugging herself in the process. “I don’t know why they haven’t faded.”

“There’s only one reason why.”

“Well that’s a bullshit reason and clearly untrue.”

“Agatha—

“I have to go pick out my spy outfit! Come stay with us later in our tension-free house!” she yelled and practically ran out of Lilia’s place.

#

Once at home, she summoned her rabbit, Señor Scratchy, into her arms and splayed out on the couch, putting on Love Island to switch off her brain. She’d had Scratchy since she was five years old. Successfully casting the familiar spell at that age had been unheard of. Agatha still remembered the pure pride that shone in her mother—Evanora’s—eyes. She’d been paraded in front of every old crone that visited Salem for three years straight just for that one spell alone.

Maybe that had triggered her thirst for magic. Her need to learn more and be able to cast impossible spells. Maybe it was the reason Agatha had sneaked into Evanora’s vault just shy of sixteen to steal the Darkhold, studying it in secret for almost two years before she was caught. To impress her mother. To show off her skill and knowledge in exchange for love and affection. That was probably what Wanda’s therapist would say. Agatha wasn’t sure as she refused to go see one herself.

She pulled Scratch to her chin like a security blanket, breathing him in. He always smelled like shortbread and custard. The comforting scent of a bakery first thing in the morning.

Wanda entered a few minutes later and quietly sat on the armchair scrolling on her phone. Usually she would’ve sat beside Agatha for a better view of the TV, but everyone kept a wide berth around Scratch. He didn’t like anyone near her, or near him, especially when Agatha needed space to breathe.

“Did you feel it?” she asked after a while. “The pulsing?”

Wanda hummed, focused on her phone. “It felt similar to my magic.”

“Similar to dark magic, too, so definitely eldritch in nature but not like a witch or a person. Maybe an artefact. At times it almost felt like a spell, though…”

“There’s nothing about it on the news.”

“Cover up to avoid a panic.”

“Which means they’ll be crawling all over Westview tomorrow.”

“Probably already are.”

Wanda worried her lip before she looked at Agatha. “You ran away again.”

Agatha pulled Scratchy closer, so tightly he kicked at her until she eased up. “We’re talking about this now? With the U.S. Army on our doorstep? They’re terrorists, Wanda. We should be hiding in our bunker.” Agatha scoffed. “And you said we wouldn’t ever have use for it.”

“I feel you might prefer detainment over talking about this.” She smiled teasingly, but couldn’t quite hide the hurt in her eyes. “I’ve been locked up in the Raft, Agatha. They know how to deal with witches there. It wasn’t fun.”

“I wasn’t running away,” Agatha mumbled. Wanda reminding her she’d been detained before only fuelled her need to go to that base later and prevent the same from happening to the coven.

“You left in the morning and was still in town late afternoon…For all I know, you weren’t coming back at all.”

“I was on my way back,” Agatha softly said.

Wanda nodded in acceptance, not arguing the semantics. How long she’d been gone wasn’t what they were talking about, but rather that she’d left at all. They were good at giving each other space. All they needed to do was ask for it. Wanda requesting Agatha stay in her bed the previous night, had instantly triggered her flight response.

“I’ve told you that I don’t care that my magic makes you horny,” Wanda said.

“I’ve told you it isn’t as simple as that.”

“Then maybe I don’t understand. You said you’re drawn to it?”

“Yes.”

“And it’s a part of me.”

“Yes.”

“So? Some people are into butts, others like breasts, maybe you’re just into magic.”

“Wanda, honey, I love that you’re trying to make this sound good and sexy, but it really isn’t.”

“I find it really hot too, you know? God, Agatha, my magic goes crazy whenever you touch me…” 

Feeling a pleasant jolt at the reminder, Agatha glanced at the time on her phone to see how long they had until they needed to go meet the coven and then caught herself, scowling at Wanda who was staring at her with twinkling eyes.

“Don’t start with me, demon.”

Wanda grinned. “I know you won’t hurt me.”

“It’s not about hurting you.”

“Then what is it?”     

Agatha wasn’t sure how to explain it. “Ever since we destroyed the Darkhold, I don’t feel like I’m me anymore.”

“We’re still healing. Still growing and settling. You constantly remind me that there’s no rush, so why aren’t you following your own advice?”

“I know that I did some pretty terrible things for a very long time…I know we made these promises to each other to be better.”

“And we are doing better.”

Agatha nodded absently. “I feel as though losing the Darkhold, I lost myself, and I haven’t really figured out how to be the person I am now. Which makes me think that it’s a bad time to be with anyone. I feel like you’re waiting for me to catch up, be at the same place you’re at, and I’m just not getting there.”

Wanda swallowed thickly. “I’m sorry for pressuring you.”

Agatha shook her head. “The pressure isn’t coming from you, Red. It’s me. I don’t know what I want. You’re still trying out new things, seeing what fits, and me? All I constantly want is the Darkhold back.”

“Oh,” Wanda breathed softly. “I didn’t realise it dominated your thoughts to that extent.”

“I didn’t say.”

“Is there anything we could do?”

“Do? Like what? Therapy? Talk about how I miss siphoning the magic from multiple witches at once? How I rapidly switch between feeling aimless and unfocused or dead inside for too many hours of the day when I’m not in my greenhouse, or with you and the coven there to distract me? Sometimes not even that helps.”

“Do you think it was a mistake to destroy it?”

“I don’t know. The book warned that any caster would eventually lose their minds to the eldritch magic. For a while I thought it was that making me feel this way. But every source I found stated that the deterioration would happen while in possession of the Darkhold, not after ridding oneself of it. And yet all I got were black fingers, since the insatiable thirst for magic and homicidal tendencies has been there since I was a teenager.”

“I think that might’ve been hormones.”

Agatha snorted in amusement but sobered soon after. “I had the Darkhold for over three centuries. Very nearly my whole life. Maybe it was the reason I was almost executed, but it was also the reason I could save myself.”

“They shouldn’t have tried to execute you at all. They could’ve taught you to control it, the way you’ve taught me.”

Agatha smiled softly, not having thought of that parallel. That she had offered Wanda the one thing she had begged her mother for whilst tied to that stake, right before Evanora had blasted her magic right into her heart.

“Do you want us to go murder a few people?” Wanda asked. “I could be into it if you need me to be.”

“You’re too good to me.”

“I know.”

“I wish it was about the murder.”

“You miss the magic of it all.”

“Yes.”

“What was it you said? You took magic from the unworthy? At the time it felt like a threat, but I think those who can't use their magic, can’t control it, are unworthy.”

“Don’t try to sugarcoat it, sugarplum. It was just something I said to make you feel insecure. My judgement on worth was severely impaired and subjective.”

“You still served a purpose.”

“Yes. My own.”

“Fair enough. Now you serve our coven and by extension this town. Sometimes I wonder if you even know how much you mean to us.”

Agatha swallowed the abrupt lump in her throat and looked to the television screen where the straights were making out in a hot tub.

“Agatha, we destroyed the Darkhold because we thought it would eventually consume you… If we can be sure it won’t hurt you, maybe we should try to get another copy?” 

Agatha must’ve squeezed Scratch again at hearing that, because he wildly wiggled in her arms and pressed his head against her throat, nearly choking her.

“I…Let me think about it,” she rasped, heart pounding in her chest. She wouldn’t even know where to begin her search. A copy of the Darkhold was hardly something you could buy online. Chances were she might never lay her eyes on even a page ever again.

Wanda turned up the volume on the television, sensing that Agatha couldn’t continue the conversation right then. The hot tub heteros had carelessly discarded a lovely bouquet of roses to the side, petals strewn everywhere.

Evanora had loved roses. The garden back in Salem had been solely maintained by her and later a little Agatha who had hung on her every word, wanting to be just like her mother when she grew up. Patience, Evanora had lectured, we need to cultivate our rose to ensure the perfect bloom. Patience, she'd said, when Agatha had wanted to learn more advanced magic too soon.

With Scratch had come the whispers and the dreams, a copy of the Darkhold locked away deep in her mother's vault desperately calling to her. When she’d been younger, she'd thought it her imagination, as it only happened every few months. But as her magic ability grew, the whispers became more frequent, more insistent. More tempting.

Patience, Agatha knew, wouldn’t make the urges go away.

#

Agatha had always been an excellent mentor. She had taught and guided hundreds of witches for over two centuries, nurturing their skills and talents like a farmer tended their sheep. Fattening them up for the slaughter.

When she’d decided to establish the Westview Coven, it was to assist Wanda in controlling the Scarlet Witch. Covens shared bonds that made it easier to tap into their magic, stabilise and increase it. Yet, as unexpected as most things in her life since she’d set foot in Westview, Agatha had unfortunately come to care for them all. Most likely another symptom of being a coven witch.

She thought of the coven like she did her roses, meant to be cultivated and grown. And like her roses, she required them to be exceptional. In a narcissistic way, Agatha relished in their successes as they were a reflection on her own skill and ability.

 Lilia’s visions had become less sporadic, her bouts of verbal outbursts she couldn’t remember the context of, less frequent. Magic users around the world were foaming at the mouth to get their hands on Jen’s potions. They were older though, and didn’t need much guidance especially based on the types of magic they wielded.

So Agatha spent most of her time focused on increasing Wanda’s control and growing Alice’s power, the coven acting as anchor and amplifier. When they’d first met, Alice had turned her back on her witch heritage and Wanda had been on the brink of destroying everything. And still, for some reason, they'd turned to Agatha for help.

Idiots.

They stood huddled in the woods on the outskirts of the response base, completing the ritual spell that would allow them to speak telepathically, Jen almost crushing Alice’s hand in worry.

‘I’ll keep her safe,’ she said to only Jen who relaxed slightly, sending Agatha a grateful look.

For decades she’d trained herself to have a mental block against mind magic. It had saved her from getting killed a few times. Which meant that now, despite being a master at channelling with a coven, she struggled with forming mental links. She had to actively keep her mind open and receptive, and often couldn’t hear the others unless she reached out to them first.

 Alice’s shroud fell over them and they walked up to the boom gate, passing through the checkpoint undetected. The place had less activity than earlier, but there was still a substantial number of armed soldiers about, guarding various tent flaps and container doors.

The three of them were dressed in jeans and leather jackets as though they rode bitch in a motorcycle gang. Still hot, but Agatha missed changing into her witch's garb. Feeling the dark purple fabric with its shadowy accents flow across her body as an extension of her power. The outfit that used to strike terror in the hearts of her enemies and victims was now a lighter shade of violet and looked and felt so wrong it made her itch being covered in it.

Worse was Wanda. Who refused to pull on that Scarlet Witch outfit, for obvious reasons Agatha fully supported her in. But what a fucking shame. Alice hadn't even bothered to try. Had said she wasn't into costumes, and fair enough. Agatha had been forced to accept that modern witches really lacked that dramatic flair. Probably due to feminism or whatever.

Now they were just a bunch of women with magic glowing in their palms and there was something very sad about it that Agatha tried not to linger on.

Wanda paused, so Agatha and Alice did too. Tilting her head, her delicious magic rose to the surface, covering her in a crimson glow. She appeared to listen for a moment and then a scene was broadcast to the coven’s mental link. Two scientists talking to a uniformed officer.

“It didn’t come from space,” one of the lab-coats said. “Footage from S.A.B.E.R. shows it appearing in Earth’s thermosphere.”

The other bespectacled scientist motioned the officer to said footage on a screen, slowed down, where a dark tear formed and a flaming object came hurtling out of it.

Wanda gently pulled out of their minds without leaving them hazy or disorientated. Perfectly in control of her magic.

Agatha’s body tingled all over. ‘That was very hot, Red.’

Wanda flushed with pride.

‘Please remember I’m in here with you,’ Alice mumbled.

‘We are too,’ came the response from Jen.

‘Your shielding is also very hot, Alice,’ Agatha said. ‘Don’t be jealous. Daddy loves you both.’

Alice rolled her eyes, grinning widely, but they all tensed when the large tent that centred the base came into view. Two guards stood in front of the entrance, though it was a tent, so everywhere was a point of entry if you had a sharp pair of scissors.  The military was run by idiots.

‘I’ve been suggesting to them that there’s nothing of interest in Westview,’ Wanda said. ‘We can do a lap around the base to get everyone, but if you want to go in now. We can.’

‘Let’s be thorough,’ Agatha said. ‘You still holding good, Alice?’

‘All good.’

They did another lap of the base, trying to find out more information while Wanda worked her suggestion spell, but everyone seemed stumped regarding the meteorite. It appeared to consist of a strange amalgamation of sedimentary, igneous, and metamorphic minerals. No organic materials, and ground-penetrating radar scans showed that it might be hollow, yet it was resistant to all ultrasonic and sonic drillers and corers they’d tried using to get a sample.

The trio circled back to the ‘entrance’ of the large tent and walked in single file between the two guards on either side of the flap. Agatha reached out her magic and suggested there was no need for them to do a check for at least an hour.

Inside, the tent covered a massive crater. Various sets of steel steps had been constructed that led down to the meteorite and spotlight posts with cameras were set up around it, sending video feed to a room on the other side of where they’d entered.

Six figures were visible through the observation window of the control room as they made their way toward them, Agatha’s attention though, was entirely on the dark spherical rock down below.

She hesitated outside when Wanda entered to put everyone to sleep and Alice went to switch off the cameras. Agatha was about to follow them inside, dragging her eyes from the sphere, when she felt an painfully familiar tug on her heart.

Her feet carried her to the nearest set of stairs, descending them in a trance, eyes fixed on the pulsing meteorite, vaguely aware of Alice and Wanda following.

She stepped up to the meteorite, her ouroboros glowing green. It was a spell. A shield barrier made of a combination of dark and chaos magic. An eldritch spell likely to be found in the Darkhold, but had never been revealed to her.

She shouldn’t touch it, and yet she placed her palm against the cool rock.

A crack formed, splintering across the sphere like branching bolts of lightning. A green glow emanated from inside. Heart furiously pounding, Agatha inhaled a shuddering breath when the feint scent of roses filled the air and the rock shell fell apart to reveal a hollow space and a woman crouched down inside of it. She wore a tight black outfit with fine green detailing. Her dark hair was gorgeously messy and hung loose around her shoulders. Barefoot, she busied herself placing two black oval shaped items—reminiscent of ostrich eggs—into a satchel bag, before she rose to her full height and shouldered the strap, turning to face her.

Rich brown eyes locked onto Agatha who stood frozen, a knot firmly lodged in her throat and tears brimming in her eyes.

“Rio?” she croaked.

Rio smiled tremulously, bowed at the waist whilst extending a hand as though she was offering something in her palm, before her luscious lips rounded and she gently blew across the glowing purple ouroboros tattoos circling her wrist. Luminous violet rose petals sprung forth, prettily showering a stunned Agatha like confetti, before Rio, her satchel of eggs, and the remnants of the shield barrier, all disappeared as though they’d never been there.

Agatha stood motionless, ears ringing in the sudden silence, warm tears leaking down her cheeks. She hadn’t thought she would ever see Rio again. And in those weak moments when she dared to consider it—needed it, craved it—Agatha had been certain that they would reunite in a clash of anger. That the familiar hatred which had come far too easily and had torn them apart, would resurface.

Instead, all Agatha felt was the two-century old ache of longing she’d fought down at every glimpse of her tattoos. Her stomach knotted, doubt creeping in as she wondered whether she had hallucinated Rio Vidal right there within touching distance.

“Agatha?” Alice asked.
Agatha’s gaze snapped toward them, twin expressions of empathy and concern confirmed that it had been real. That Rio had really been there.

“I have to go.” Her voice cracked and she teleported home.

 

Chapter 3: The Alien Invasion

Her mind had locked up on instinct, severing the mental link. The coven didn’t try to contact her, instead giving her time and space to spiral in her bed in peace. Agatha heard them coming home with Wanda, loudly whispering in the living room downstairs before retiring to their usual spots. Jen and Alice to the guest room and Lilia to Wanda’s room. The sounds of them settling-in faded and Agatha’s mind re-centred back to earlier.

Back to Rio.

Two hundred years and Rio crashes into her town, appearing inside of a magical barrier that was drenched in eldritch magic. And she hadn’t been in the meteorite the whole time. Agatha had felt the exact moment she’d arrived, which meant that Rio had been there to collect those black egg-shaped things. That she might have left after retrieving them and those few seconds of seeing her were all Agatha would get.

The urge to use her ouroboros to feel for Rio was overwhelming, but Agatha resisted, centuries of denial and stubbornness aiding her in not giving in.

More unsettling than seeing her again, than not being able to muster even an ounce of the anger she’d felt when they’d parted, was the knowledge that Rio wasn’t one to cause a scene. Well, Rio loved to cause a scene, but not on such a grand scale. Certainly not to draw that type of attention.

And then to smile at Agatha the way she had…after everything.

Agatha groaned into her pillow but stiffened when her bedroom door cracked open. She had her back to it and light from the hallway filtered in, shining a spotlight on her. Usually when everyone was over, Wanda shared with Agatha.

“Agatha?” she whispered and Agatha’s chest clenched painfully.

The door closed and she could feel Wanda in the room with her. Felt her getting into bed. Felt the arms that wrapped around her and the fingers soothingly stroking her hair. Agatha sighed wetly and lost herself in the gentle buzz of Wanda’s magic, having mentally and emotionally exhausted herself enough to fall asleep.

#

She woke up just shy of noon, alone, and loved Wanda more for it.

After dressing in workout clothes—leggings, a sport bra and a long loose purple tank—and pulling her hair into a messy ponytail, she made her way downstairs, intent on going for a run.

She found the entire coven in the living room, Billy included, all dumbly staring at the news. Alien Invasion? It read on the headline strip below the news anchor before the feed switched to a giant obsidian fortress, various species of Undead creatures flying between tall towers and over high walls. An army of a thousand black armoured Undead stood in a vast courtyard.

The fortress was encircled by a two-hundred-foot-wide ravine, so deep, the drone footage couldn’t capture the bottom of it from the sky.

“What the…” Agatha whispered. What was Rio doing? It had to be her. But why? “Where is that?”

“Smack in the centre of West and Eastview,” Billy said. “It has a shield around it. A news chopper exploded flying into it. A few drones too. There were another few random explosions. Reddit thinks they were missiles but no one has admitted anything.”

Agatha rubbed her brow and thanked Alice when a steamy mug of coffee was pressed into her hand.

“Agatha.” She looked up at Lilia awkwardly fiddling with her fingers. “We know you had a shock last night, but…” She trailed off and seemed to give up.

Jen stared at Lilia as though there had been a discussion that Lilia would ask and then bailed at the last second. Jen being Jen, stepped up instead. “Is your ex-wife trying to kill us?”

Agatha gulped down her too hot coffee. She’d thought many things after seeing that fortress. Rio wanting to kill them hadn’t made the list.

“No,” she said. “Rio wouldn’t.”

“Are you sure?” Alice hesitantly asked. “Because…” She motioned to the fortress, straight out of an evil villain handbook.

“She’s just into that whole aesthetic.”

Jen scoffed. “Oh, so it’s a cosmetic choice that she displaced half of the woods to put down a castle fortress and summoned her demon army in through portals.”

“How do you know they were summoned through portals?”

“They have footage of it happening earlier.”

“Is it only happening here?”

“As far as we know,” said Billy.

Agatha finished her coffee, rolling her burnt tongue around in her mouth for a moment.

“We should just leave her be,” she mumbled and went to place her mug in the kitchen. There was silence behind her as she grabbed a blueberry muffin, unsurprised to find everyone gaping in disbelief when she returned to the living room.

“Lilia, lets supercharge you,” she said and bit into her muffin. “Find out if we have anything to worry about.”

Lilia, thankfully, did not mention the falling into an endless void vision, which fair enough might be unrelated, but probably not. They pushed the furniture aside, the coven seemingly grateful to be doing something. Wanda had been quiet throughout the conversation and Agatha had avoided eye contact.

Still, they pressed their shoulders together once seated on the floor in the circle the coven formed. Billy handed Lilia a pen and notepad and sat down next to her.

Agatha extended her hands, taking Wanda and Jen’s on either side. They were all still linked from the evening before, so it was easy to connect, their magic flowing through them like rolling currents. Closing her eyes, Agatha opened her mind and her magic, and led them through the incantation.

Sentire nos sororem sicut te sentimus.

Estote fortior nobis, sicut et nos fortes sumus vobis.

 The spell weaved through them, and Agatha gathered the coven’s magic, gently channelling it toward Lilia. Their voices blended into a pleasant hum, aiding her focus. It was the closest Agatha got to siphoning these days. Strangely enough, she’d never had the urge to consume the coven’s magic like she did Wanda’s, easily guiding multiple streams to encourage and empower Lilia’s visions. Trying to ignore the way the chaos magic warmed her belly as it passed through her.

An indiscernible time later, though Billy most likely had a timer running since he took notes of everything, they felt Lilia break the chain. Agatha’s eyes fluttered open, all of them pleasantly dazed as they watched Lilia scribbling on the notepad. No one said a word, leaning against each other like drugged up hippies at Woodstock. Agatha had so much sex and drugs in August of ‘69 she was surprised she remembered any of it.

While she contemplated sending Billy home and suggesting an orgy, Lilia finished writing and then placed the pad in the centre of their little circle. Well, at least that stopped the magic-high induced thought short. They were more of a lets-go-karaoke than a lets-go-have-group-sex type of coven anyway.

Predictably, Lilia had scribbled down a load of nonsense. A simple list with three columns containing dates, objects, and places. Painting, Ladle, Disc, Carpet, Vase, Tablet, Head. All seven items had the present day’s date beside them citing various cities around the world. The last three all said London. The eighth entry on Lilia’s list was for the next day, followed by House, Hewlett Harbour - Mystery.

The fortress shield covered a half-mile radius, and Agatha approached it from the Eastview side, through the forest, to avoid being anywhere near the response base that had grown disturbingly in size since the previous evening. There were tanks, armoured vehicles with heavy artillery, squadrons of soldiers and a few sleek black SUVs that unsettled her the most.

No, she wouldn’t give Rio—who decided that it was just fine to flip her world upside down and then vanish without a word—the satisfaction.

Shit.

She had no desire to use that shaky looking bridge over a pit of darkness, especially not with Lilia’s void vision playing in the back of her mind, so they cast a group teleportation in full view of a platoon of giant armoured Undead carrying spears and swords with glowing green blades.

Rio left the centrepiece of the greenhouse for last, and made her way toward the large black blooms with their green tipped edges and Agatha’s stomach fluttered in anticipation. Rio reverently ran a finger down a tall stem, heedless of the sharp thorns. It had taken Agatha decades to get the perfect proportions. To get a specimen with the looks of a hybrid tea rose and the fragrant potency of the old garden roses she’d grown up with. The colour though, green roses were rare and often a pale olive rather than the vibrant harlequin green Rio loved. Agatha had painstakingly bred with the greenest mutations she could get her hands on and finally nailed it. After centuries of compulsive propagation.

“Oh, Agatha…you did it,” she whispered, carefully touching a petal and the rosebud opened and bloomed for her, like Rio was the sun. “They’re perfect...”

Agatha preened, her heart growing full. Last Rio had seen them, they were a different variant, the stems too thin to carry the heads and they kept drooping and dying prematurely, growing in too large bushes instead of the elegant single stem she’d been striving for.

Agatha cleared her throat. “Nuestra Señora de la Santa Muerte,” she said. Rio grinned, amused and utterly delighted. Agatha shrugged sheepishly. “Holy Deaths for short. I’m not known for my imagination.”

Seeing her like this, in this time period, was so surreal and yet somehow Rio blended perfectly whilst still being so completely and implicitly herself.

“You called for me?” Rio softly said.

“You forgot to fill your moat,” Agatha mumbled.

“I didn’t want to displace that much water.”

Agatha hummed.

“What do you want, Agatha?”

“Is it bad? Whatever's happening?”

Rio’s shoulders curled. “Yes. But I'm handling it.”

Agatha nodded. “Do I need to take the coven away?”

Rio swallowed and shook her head. “The fortress will be the safest place should it come to that.”

“Thank you,” she rasped, taking a careful step closer, because she couldn't stop herself. “Can I help in any way?”

“I've got it handled,” Rio told the ground, her hands leaving her pockets.

She looked exhausted, worried, and Agatha slowly reached out to cup her cheek. Aching when Rio gently grasped her wrist, and turned her face to press a lingering kiss to Agatha’s palm, and another to the green dragon covering her wrist, causing a shiver up Agatha’s spine. Rio’s eyes briefly fell shut at Agatha’s physical response to her. A single tear escaped her lashes and rolled down her cheek, onto Agatha’s tattoo.

Agatha wrapped her in a hug before she knew she was going to.

Rio melted into her, and Agatha cupped the back of her head, cradled her into her neck. Smelled her hair, and remembered how no rose had ever been able to come close to Rio’s scent. Agatha had tried. Had been trying for centuries to replicate her smell. But Rio’s rosy scent contained hints of amber and papyrus that added a woodsy warmth Agatha doubted she’d ever be able to organically reproduce.

So she breathed her in and held her close. Focused on Rio’s hands tightly gripping her back, desperately clinging to her. And tried to remember why she had ever allowed things to spiral so tragically between them. How she’d ever thought she hated Rio. How she could ever say those horrible things she’d said and still have Rio there holding her back like a lifeline.

“Agatha?” Wanda's voice sounded from outside and Rio stiffened in her arms then jerked out of the embrace, causing a wave of cold to wash over Agatha. Deep brown eyes shimmered with hurt and betrayal, Rio’s fists clenched and expression wounded.

“Sorry,” Agatha rasped through a thick throat and painfully clenching chest.

Rio tried and failed to smile, her lips wobbling.

Tears fell across Agatha’s cheeks at the melancholy sight.

“Please don’t go,” Agatha whispered, her voice cracking. Needing to explain. What, she wasn’t sure, but she couldn’t let Rio leave again. Not after hurting her, again.

Rio closed her eyes as though in agony, blindly pulled her knife, and disappeared even as Agatha reached out to try and stop her.

“Alice found something,” Wanda said, sounding hesitant, not making any attempt to enter.

‘I'll be there in a minute,’ Agatha replied telepathically so she could regulate her voice. Her chest and throat too tight to form a verbal response.

And at Wanda's retreating footsteps, Agatha pressed a hand to her mouth, lowered to the floor, and silently shook with sobs amongst her roses.

Chapter 4: The Long Island Mystery

“Did you change your clothes?” Jen asked, brows knitted when Agatha entered the living room twenty minutes later, having used magic to clean her face and remove the puffiness from her eyes.
