Agatha snorted. “Trust me, hon. The only one in danger here of getting killed by either of you, is me.”

Wanda smiled softly. “I talked your ear off about Vis for years and you listened and supported me through it. That helped me to keep a place for him in my heart and still be strong enough to move on. I mourned Billy and Tommy, and you confided in me about Nicky. I know his favourite colour was purple like your magic, and that he was the one who wrote the original Ballad. I know of the time he accidentally rolled off the bed and you cried louder than he did.” She chuckled when Agatha cringed at the memory. “But I didn't even know Rio’s name, Agatha. And I remember asking you about her and you would just clamp up as though in pain and for a while I thought maybe she’d been abusive—

“No. Never.”

Wanda sighed. “You need to go deal with whatever you two didn’t deal with back then. I’ll be right here and support you while you do. Not for us to be together. Not to be good. But because you are my best friend and I need you to be happy, like you have helped me become a happier person these last few years. Maybe you’ll discover what it is that’s feeling off for you at the moment.”

Agatha doubted Rio would listen to a word she had to say. Not that she could say anything that would change the way they’d left things.

“I love you,” she whispered. It sounded like manipulation, but it was the only truth she felt confident in telling Wanda in that moment. “And I’ll try.”

Wanda smiled sadly. “I love you, too.”

#

Squished into the minivan they’d bought for road trips—heading to New York to get drunk and dance—the coven had to magic their way past multiple roadblocks monitoring traffic in and out of Westview. When Alice pulled up to the suburban home in Eastview, Agatha turned in the front seat to look at a pouting Billy behind her.

“Here’s your stop, kid.”

He looked hurt more than disappointed. Agatha knew he had some insecurities over his lack of magic, but they were heading to an unknown house for an unknown reason and Rio had assembled her Legion which meant the threat was real and dangerous, so Agatha needed him to stay safe.

“I could wait in the car and be the getaway driver,” Billy suggested.

“You could, or you could stay here and spend time with your parents who you barely see anymore, before you go off to college.”

“They told me to go and enjoy my summer.”

Everyone was quiet, not offering any input, despite agreeing with her.

“Do you know what I was doing at your age?” Agatha asked.

“Walking barefoot in the snow for five miles to get to school?”

Agatha smiled sharply. “Killing my entire coven. Including my mother, who tried to kill me when I didn’t turn out to be who she wanted me to be.”

“Oh.”

The tension in the van grew thick. Only Wanda’s soft gaze was still on Agatha after that statement. It wasn’t new information to anyone, but Agatha liked to mention it on occasion and bask in the awkwardness that followed.

There had been a time where Agatha’s relationship with her mother had been good. Back when Agatha had been perceived as good. Back when she'd bent herself over backwards to be someone her mother could show off like one of her prised roses. Perfectly cultivated. William Kaplan had only ever experienced unconditional love. Hadn’t ever needed to try and be someone he wasn’t. And Agatha hoped with all of her heart that he would never need to.

“We want you around, Billy.” She softened her tone. “You’re a member of this coven, but for the love of god, go be with your family while they no doubt stare at the news and wonder where you are and if you’re safe. We’ll come pick you up when we’re back. All right?”

Billy sighed and shifted forward, placing a kiss on her cheek. “Love you.”

“Love you too, handsome,” Agatha murmured. “Tell your hot mom I said hi.”

He snorted a chuckle even as he tried to glare at her and Agatha settled back in her seat and watched him until he was inside.

When the front door shut, they all raised their hands, palms up, and Alice softly chanted a protection spell around the Kaplan home.

#

They made it to Long Island before noon taking the I-95. Jen and Lilia napped for most of the journey, but woke when they reached Hempstead. Billy, bless him, had used Google Maps’ street viewer to find their destination. The village was small, and not many streets went up to 169, so it hadn’t taken long for Lilia to identify the house she’d seen in her vision.

“What now?” Jen asked when they were very conspicuously parked across the street.

Agatha shrugged, eyes darting across the Victorian home painted a charcoal grey with ivory highlights, standing out amongst a row of identical brownstones, like it didn’t quite belong. She tapped in the address and it didn’t seem to be a heritage site, so remarkable really to not have been turned into a bland piece of real estate by an HOA in the name of modern conformity.

“We should go in,” Lilia said.

“I’ll go in,” Agatha countered. “You guys wait here.”

They all huffed and rolled their eyes and exited the van with her.

‘What was that you said about them trusting me?’ Agatha asked Wanda.

‘They trust you to not ask for help when you need it.’

Agatha sighed, smoothed down the marvellous dusty-blue coat she’d dressed in that morning. Her hair pinned up, and her locket resting against the crisp white shirt that covered her chest. Her coven had all verbalised their appreciation of the outfit. Jen had tried to upstage her dressed in pink from head to toe like cotton candy, and fine, she looked good, but Agatha was convinced she’d won that round. It helped to get her out of her emotional funk and feel confident enough to go find out whatever Lilia’s visions wanted them to know.

A few feet up the pathway she paused at the gentle tug at her heart, and groaned.

“What?” Jen asked.

“Rio just got here.”

“Okay,” Wanda said. “Guess we’re at the right place, then.” She lifted a brow at Agatha and motioned for her to lead the way.

Rolling her eyes, Agatha entered the house through the unlocked front door and came to a grinding halt. Vaguely aware of the door being closed, and the others swearing at her for blocking the way, shuffling passed to flank her.

They stood in a large foyer with a high ceiling, the most notable feature a grandiose crystal chandelier. Previously the most notable feature actually as Rio currently levitated beside it seemingly affixing a light bulb. Seemingly affixing a light bulb in a black strapless sheath dress. A formal strapless sheath dress with a long slit where a black lace garter belt held up by dainty suspenders was peeking out.

Agatha’s breath caught, taking in the dark red lipstick, Rio’s hair elegantly pinned at her nape, glittering diamonds in her ears and around her elegant neck, and long silky gloves coming up over her elbows. She looked gorgeous and Agatha absently unbuttoned her coat with one hand.

She missed playing dress-up with Rio. They always had a grand time. She had to actively suppress the urge to change into a 1950’s style tuxedo.

Rio’s stilettos hit the hardwood floor, probably damaging it, but she didn’t seem to care as she drew an ugly rug from thin air and laid it below the chandelier.

“Pazyryk rug. St. Petersburg,” Alice whispered, eyes trained on Rio’s ass when she bent over and straightened out the tattered rug.

Rio heard her, because of course she did, smirking to herself and straightened, an opera-length, ivory cigarette holder appeared in her gloved hand, the mouthpiece pressed between her teeth. Rio slyly grinned around it as her dark gaze drank Agatha in.

Agatha stood taller at the appreciative look her outfit garnered, pleased at the wardrobe choices she’d made at three in the morning, unable to sleep.

Rio sauntered closer, straight toward her. “Hello, Agatha’s Coven,” she said, not looking at anyone other than Agatha. Heedless of the awkwardly mumbled greetings that were returned.

“Darling,” Rio purred in a deep southern accent, wrist going to her forehead, and it was pure muscle memory that drove Agatha to catch Rio as she feigned delicately fainting in her arms. Rich brown eyes darkened when Agatha kept her bent in a low dip, a hand lightly gripped the back of Rio’s stocking covered knee and slid upward to brush across the lace before lightly tugging a thumb beneath a thin suspender, palm curling around a warm thigh.

Rio ran her tongue across her teeth. “Did I trip? Did I stumble—lose my balance, graze my knee, graze my heart?”

Agatha smiled, staring at the chords straining in Rio’s exquisite neck, before she lifted her upright, Rio’s arms falling around her shoulders with practised ease. Gazing at Agatha as though she would devour her on the spot. Agatha had been gone the second she’d seen Rio in that dress. She had no defences in place against a silly-sexy Rio combo.

Thankfully, someone cleared their throat. Possibly Lilia. Agatha woke from her stupor, face on fire, her stomach and chest too. Rio poked her tongue to the inside of her cheek, staring at Agatha’s mouth, then mercifully stepped back and out of Agatha’s hands possessively gripping her hips.

‘Sorry about that,’ Agatha said to Wanda, unable to look at her.

Wanda didn’t reply.

 “So wonderful to see you all again. And so soon!” Rio smiled warmly at them. “Now, please leave.” She motioned grandly to the front door, then lithely twirled on her heels. The Ife Head stolen from the British Museum appeared in her hands that she placed on a Burmese carved elephant side table, dead centre and facing an identical head and table on the opposite side. She then headed out of the entrance hall and further into the house.

Agatha pushed a hand into her pocket while her gaze followed Rio all the way out. She then rocked on her heels and lifted her brows when she felt the heavy stares on her.

“Well,” she said, when no one else said anything. “Time to leave. Vamanos!”

She spun around to the front door.

Nobody moved.

Agatha shut her eyes, fingers curled on the ornate brass handle. She sighed, turned, and walked in the direction Rio had gone, finding her in the kitchen where she placed the stolen hishaku beside a Sen no Rikyū tea set, carefully lining it up beside the tray.

“So…” Agatha said. “Are you moving in?”

“No.” Rio deadpanned and stalked out of the room.

Agatha trailed after her, deciding to enjoy the view while she allowed enough time to pass for the coven to think she tried and then be more willing to leave.

“Still a pervert I see,” Rio murmured.

Agatha smirked and followed her to a baroque style bedroom, all dark burgundy and rosewood. Rio gracefully stepped onto the mattress and mounted Van Gogh’s Starry Night above the bed. Spending a long moment straightening it to perfectly align with the headboard. She then walked back to where Agatha leaned against the door frame.

“Agatha, if you continue to stalk me, I will call the police,” Rio drawled and brushed passed her. Agatha impulsively inhaled, all but floating after her where the pilfered Sophilos Vase was placed on a mahogany Edwardian side table. Rio turned it carefully until the Fates, Graces and Muses were facing to the front.

“You're currently on every Most Wanted list in the world,” Agatha said, consumed by curiosity as to what Rio was up to. “So I’m certain they'll be happy to hear from you.”

“What do you want, Agatha?”

“Just supervising the coven while they’re investigating you.”

“I would prefer they stop.”

“I have requested multiple times that they do.”

“They think I'm the threat.” A statement, but Agatha still nodded. “Seriously, you can’t be here.”

“Okay, just let them feel like they did something today. Then we'll go.”

Rio placed the Rosetta Stone at the top of the staircase, adjusting it so the stele stood perfectly centre of the landing.

“Wanda and I aren’t together.”

“So just fucking her then,” Rio blandly said. “She’s pretty. Could destroy the entire universe if you break her heart, so making sound choices as always, Agatha. We both know what you do to the people who love you when things don’t go your way.”

“Spare me the lecture. I know who I was—who I am. I guess…”

“A dirty cheater is what you are,” Rio said. “Since my creator married us, we’ll need to go see them if you want a divorce. You’ve already rendered our vows meaningless.”

“I didn’t ask for a divorce,” Agatha said, heart in her throat. “Do you want one? And I’ve never met your creator. Your brother married us. ”

Rio stiffened. “Yes he did. I misspoke.”

It was an odd mistake for Rio to make, but the divorce talk was making her queasy so Agatha decided not to focus on that. “How is your brother anyway?”

“Dead.”

“Your sister?”

“Dead.”

“Fuck.”

“Yes. I'm the only member left of the Living Tribunal.”

“So that’s what all of this is about.”

“Yes.”

“I'm sorry, Rio. I know you were close with them.”

“Thanks.”

“You still can’t die, right? That hasn’t changed?”

“No, I get to live forever and watch everyone I love die over and over again.”

Agatha swallowed thickly, clutching her locket. “Rio—

Rio was suddenly too close to her, up in her space. “I want you to stop talking and leave, Agatha. I don’t want anything from you. I don’t want you near me. I don’t want you to halfheartedly tell me how you’re not in a relationship with the woman you’re fucking. I don’t care.”

“You don’t care?”

“I don’t care if you go on another two hundred year fuckfest around the world. You won’t ever get me out of your system. You will never be able to erase what we are to each other. But if you continue to flaunt it in my face, I will fucking kill you.”

Agatha slowly smirked, closed the inch left between them to press her body against Rio’s. Eyes hooded as she stared at Rio’s blood red lips. “God, I missed you...”

Rio rolled her eyes, trying to hide a smile as she placed her fingers against Agatha’s sternum and pushed her away.

Agatha licked her lips, but stepped back, trying to ignore the warmth that spread where Rio had touched her. “I’m not flaunting anything.”

“You’re literally stalking me with your fuckbuddy.”

“Rio, come on—

The lights around the house flickered and for a moment Agatha thought it was Lilia’s magic, but she didn’t feel Lilia casting and then Rio swore under her breath and disappeared.

“What did you do!” Rio’s angry voice sounded from somewhere below.

Agatha teleported to the foyer then ran toward the opulent living area where the coven defensively grouped together, staring down a furious looking Rio.

“Who lights a fucking fireplace during summer!” Rio shouted.

Baffled, Agatha walked forward, standing in between Rio and her coven, tilting her head at her friends.

“What did you do?” she directed at them, gaze trained on the fear in Rio’s eyes, the tension in her shoulders.

As though feeling exposed, a dark cloak formed across Rio’s body, a hood settling over her head. A familiar satchel was placed over her shoulder and protectively hugged to her body. It looked empty. Flat. But had done so even after Rio had placed those weird eggs inside of it.

“Hey, we’ll put out the fire,” Jen said, frowning whilst glaring. “Ali’s a bit of a pyromaniac when she gets bored.” She looked to Agatha. “We were just waiting around for you two to be done with whatever it was you were doing.”

“It’s already started,” Rio said, her knife appearing in her hand, clenched in a white knuckled grip. “I can’t stop it or move you now.”

Everything around them disappeared. The entire house gone. Vanishing so abruptly that it took everyone a moment to register that they now stood on a smooth flat platform surrounded by glittering stars and brilliant galaxies, as though they were in space.

Behind Rio, casting her in a silhouette, a large blue moon illuminated them. Unnervingly close.

“This is all your fault,” Rio told Agatha and then the platform vanished too.

Agatha’s stomach bottomed out and then she was falling, the coven’s screams filling her head, everything around her a void of endless nothingness, even though her eyes were opened wide and terrified.

Chapter 5: The Far Shore

They fell for minutes that felt like hours, screaming until their voices grew hoarse. A million thoughts rushed through Agatha’s mind, and yet all she could focus on was the worry of what it would mean should they finally hit the ground after such a long fall. Would this be how she lost them? Because she wasn’t more insistent that they heed Rio’s warnings?

Rio was right. This was all her fault. Somehow the witch-killer had managed to wipe-out yet another coven.

‘When you’re all quite done,’ Rio’s voice rumbled in their heads cutting off the screams. ‘Kindly remember that you’re witches and stop falling.’

Delirious with relief, Agatha laughed, purple lighting up below green glowing wrists as she cast the flying spell. The others followed as twin balls of yellow, red, orange, and pink joined her. They grouped together using the colourful light of their magic as their bodies remained eerily swallowed by the void.

“Good,” Rio said out loud.

A lantern appeared in her hand, illuminating them in a green glow, and they all became visible. Agatha’s hair had somehow sprung loose from confinement and she ran a hand through it trying to calm her rapid breaths. Everyone looked a little haggard. Jen and Alice were mid embrace, pressing soft kisses to each other’s faces and everyone discreetly looked away. Agatha leaned into the hug when Lilia wrapped an arm around her waist and gave it a little squeeze. 

After allowing them a moment to settle their heart rates, Rio spoke again. “Stay in my light.”

Everyone turned their attention to her, intently listening, noticing her seemingly standing on some invisible path. Wanda was the first to land on it.

“It’s best you conserve your magic,” Rio said, nodding at Wanda in approval and everyone else followed, shakily landing on nothing but air. It felt solid, like a linoleum surface, and because they couldn’t see anything, was extremely disorientating.

“I’ll keep the road up until we reach our destination.” Rio then turned and headed into the dark void.

Alice and Jen behind her, Lilia behind them, and Wanda fell into step beside Agatha who brushed the back of their hands together. Relieved that everyone was alive and unharmed.

“Where, exactly, is our destination?” Agatha hoarsely asked.

“The Far Shore,” Rio said in a tone that told Agatha she was still angry they were there at all and she decided to hold her questions until they were in a safer place.

Thankfully, everyone else seemed to agree.

#

They walked for hours. Nothing but void around them. And then Alice started humming an all too familiar tune. Jen and Lilia joined in on the opening verse of the Ballad of the Witches’ Road and Wanda reached out to take Agatha’s hand.

The coven had their first bonding experience breaking a generational curse on Alice. Her mother’s version had acted as a spell to prevent the curse from taking complete hold of her daughter.

 They knew that Agatha had made up the Road. Knew the Ballad was how she’d tricked hundreds of witches out of their magic and their lives. It had become somewhat of an inside joke. But none save Wanda was aware of the shame that plagued Agatha. Not because of the witches she’d killed, but because she’d used her son’s song to aid her in doing so. And because it held such emotional significance to Alice too, Agatha never said anything.

“Stop,” Rio's gruff whisper reverberated around them and they instantly fell silent and stilled when Rio stopped walking.

Agatha stared at Rio’s rigid back. Could feel the others looking to her for guidance, probably afraid they were going to be left behind in the void.

Rio started walking again and the coven released a breath, moving in tandem to keep pace with her.

“Sorry, Rio,” Alice said.

“You may talk, you may hum, you may sing. Just not that song,” Rio softly said. “Sorry for overreacting.”

“No, it’s cool,” Alice mumbled. “You’re cool…”

No one talked or hummed or sang though, only kept their eyes on Rio, following her for hours on end until their bodies ached and their throats were parched. Not a complaint was voiced and a collective sigh of relief was released when they stepped onto a solid rocky surface.

The area they entered looked like a massive cave. Agatha nearly moaned when her straining muscles finally relaxed, releasing the tension held in fear of being swallowed by the void. Green light filled the cavern that was about fifty feet high and seventy across, revealing jagged edges on the sides. Ahead, a solid arch was carved into stone, shaped like a doorway with various runes chiselled across its smooth surface, though without a handle or any slits to show it could be entered through.

Perhaps because of the sudden uneven ground, Jen took a step and tripped, crying out in pain, and Alice caught her before she could face plant.

“Shit.” Jen sucked in a sharp breath through her teeth, limping in Alice’s arms, who carefully assisted her to the side of the cave to sit on a small boulder.

The coven gathered around her in concern, but it was Rio who moved forward her lantern left to hang from a metal hook—that hadn’t been there before—beside the arch, still illuminating the entire cavern.

Rio knelt down in front of Jen and everyone tensed.

“May I?” she asked, staring up at Jen through her long dark lashes and Agatha’s jaw clenched when Jen all but swooned and mutely nodded.

Rio carefully removed one of Jen’s ridiculous heels and someone gasped at the blisters littering her feet.

“You’re bleeding,” Alice croaked, kneeling beside Jen who continued to stare at Rio gently holding her ankle.

Jen hadn’t complained once during their hours long walk.

“You should’ve said,” Agatha muttered.

Jen scoffed. “And what? Take a break over absolute nothingness? No thanks.”

“May I use my magic on you?” Rio asked, examining the damage.

Jen looked to Agatha, who stiffly nodded, then softly gave her permission.

The second Rio’s fingers touched her skin, Jen let out a long languid moan, head lolling back, and Agatha’s stomach clenched in memory of how good Rio could make her healing feel. Now Jen was feeling all the good stuff, while Agatha wanted to murder someone. Mostly Rio, because there was really no need for all of that.

“All good?” Rio husked.

Jen’s chest heaved as she sheepishly smiled down at her. “Uh, yeah. Thanks.”

Rio nodded and got to her feet. ‘I’m going to revenge fuck your entire coven,’ she snarled into Agatha’s head, then said out loud, “I’ll be right back. Don’t go anywhere.” And vanished before a glowering Agatha could strangle her.

“Where does she think we would possibly go?” Lilia wondered, staring out into the abyss beyond the green light.

“If looks could kill,” Wanda muttered and Agatha realised she was glaring daggers at Jen still blissed out on the boulder, Alice beside her looking grumpy and confused.

“Uhm,” Jen said, finally noting Alice’s demeanour. “I could make some water?”

Everyone perked up at that.

“But…” She cast her spell, water gathering into a small sphere above her palm. “We don’t have anything to pour it into.”

“I’m not drinking from your hands,” Lilia said.

“The water doesn’t actually sprout from my body, you witch. Alchemy involves the transmutation of matter and laid the foundation for modern chemistry—

“I’ll make glasses,” Wanda said.

“And chairs,” Lilia said. “Add a table too.”

“Why do we need a table?”

“So I can rest my elbows on it.”

Wanda rolled her eyes and a dining table, chairs, and glasses floated into existence.

“Even out the ground first, dear,” Lilia said. “I'm not tipping off a chair and breaking a limb, however orgasmic Rio’s healing magic appears to be.”

Wanda snorted, Jen’s eyes glazed over, and Alice and Agatha scowled.

Done with all of them, Agatha walked to a boulder on the other side of the cavern and sat down, summoned Scratchy into her lap, and longed for the mountains.

She hadn’t allowed herself to focus on the danger they were in. Rio had been insistent that they leave, and now they were there. They had a rule that Agatha wouldn’t ask about matters of the universe. Not because Rio didn’t want to tell her, but there were things that humans on her particular Earth weren’t meant to know about. That no mortal should know about. There were rules to follow.

Rio wouldn’t leave them there, would she? She’d left Agatha for two centuries, though. But why bother guiding them to solid ground only to abandon them thereafter?

From the corner of her eye, she spotted Alice reaching out to Rio’s green lantern.

“I wouldn’t touch that if I were you,” Agatha said, and Alice jumped back, raised her hands and eyebrows, and promptly made her way back to the others.

“Can you make food?” Jen asked Wanda who still had the furniture hovering in the air surrounded in a red glow. “I’m starving.”

“Yep. What would you like?”

“That doesn't seem quite right to consume,” Alice said.

“What do you mean?” Wanda frowned. “We're about to drink Jen's hand water.”

The other three remained dubious.

Wanda looked to her. “Agatha, where does my food magic come from?”

“Since there aren’t any ingredients laying about, it would come from the power of an evil eldritch god obsessed with black magic and world domination.”

Lilia hummed. “Definitely not kosher.”

“It's not hand water,” Jen muttered under her breath.

“I’m sorry I lit that fire guys,” Alice blurted.

Jen shook her head. “Yes, like you knew lighting a fireplace would lead to all of this.”

“I’m not going to apologise for having visions,” Lilia said. “Make a toilet too, Wanda dear.”

Alice shoulders relaxed. “Can’t believe I’m this thirsty while my bladder’s so full.”

Wanda rolled her eyes and a red portable toilet appeared off to the side on the flattest surface around.

“Wow, like we’re at a concert,” Jen drawled, eyeing it with distaste.

“It’s perfect, Wanda,” Alice said, moving toward it but Lilia quickly bypassed her and entered.

Dragging her gaze from the now occupied port-a-potty, Alice sheepishly turned to Jen. “I wouldn’t mind drinking like that. Wanda might be a while.”

Wanda was studying the ground intently, appearing not to have heard her.

Jen’s lips parted when Alice took her wrist, mechanically casting the spell. Alice then bent at the waist and lapped at the water running across her fingers while Jen looked seconds away from spontaneously combusting.

Lilia exited with a relieved sigh, drying her hands on a sheet of paper towel, brow lifted in Alice and Jen’s direction.

“I don’t want to mess with the ground in case we start falling again!” Wanda groaned and covered her eyes with her hands the table and chairs wildly circling in the air above her.

“Good thinking,” Rio said, having appeared out of nowhere carrying multiple bags of takeout.

Everyone stilled and stared at her. Lilia with her hand on the port-a-potty door midway to closing it, Jen where she was stiffly holding her fingers out to Alice who remained bent, facing Rio as water splashed against her cheek, and Wanda who had subconsciously frozen all of her furniture in the air.

Only Scratchy moved. Leaping off Agatha’s lap, his body enveloped in shadowy purple as he flew thirty feet through the air. Rio carelessly dropped the food and caught him in her arms, grinning madly as she twirled him around.

“Hola señor,” she murmured into his fur, everyone so still and quiet that it was easy to hear her. Scratch released a string of chittering noises, body wriggling in excitement.

Agatha swallowed thickly.

At age five, Scratchy had been an excellent name to choose for a rabbit familiar. He’d only become Señor Scratchy after they’d met Rio.

“Yo también te extrañé, muchacho.” Rio’s fond tone echoed through the silence. “Lo sé, lo sé, lo siento.” She tenderly nuzzled his head, rubbed her cheek against his fur with her eyes closed.

She then paused, her eyes flashed open, blankly taking in everyone staring at her. “Let’s talk privately, mijo,” she said, turned her back to them, sat criss-cross on the ground, where a dome of rock covered them instantly.

Agatha stared at Rio's rocky dome, aching all over. Feeling the burn of eyes on her, she looked up into Wanda's soft gaze.

“Uhm,” Alice said. “Do you think the food’s for us?” she asked Agatha who shrugged and motioned for her to grab it. Not like Rio needed to eat, so she’d most likely gotten it for them.

The table and chairs were placed onto the wobbly ground and Wanda added plates and cutlery.

“Sit down and enjoy your last supper, children,” Lilia drawled. “Good thing we have a table.” She pointedly stared at Wanda who chuckled while she opened a can of soda and had to cover it with her palm to stop the fizz spraying out.

The coven settled around the table, packing out food, quiet in their ravenous hunger, until Jen gasped, lifting a shoebox containing a pair of pink Balenciaga sneakers that perfectly matched the colour of her outfit.

“I’m going to marry that witch,” Jen said, sounding close to tears as she magically cleaned her feet, slid on the socks, and then slipped her feet into the ridiculous shoes with a contented groan.

 Agatha remained on her boulder and stared at the rock Scratch and Rio were entombed in. Rio had always been generous and attentive. She was good at picking up on Agatha’s moods and guessing what she might need when Agatha hadn’t even known herself. Rio’s ability to be an absolute menace with sociopathic tendencies only added to the fact that she’d been the perfect wife.

“Come eat, Agatha,” Lilia said.

Agatha wasn't hungry, but everyone was staring at her with concern, so she got up and joined them at the table.

Rio had gotten a lot of different options. Chinese, Mexican, fried chicken with salads, burgers, and fries. There was even a container of what used to be sushi yet had been jostled apart when Rio had dropped the bags. It didn’t stop Jen from unwrapping a set of chopsticks and digging in.

Agatha’s stomach twisted, but she placed a fry into her mouth after Wanda pushed a plate of food in front of her. They were probably going to need their energy for whatever was coming next.

“I don't think I've ever heard Señor Scratchy make those noises before,” Alice carefully said.

“They’ve always been close,” Agatha murmured, staring unseeing at her plate. Then smiled to herself. “They both like hissing at people.”

Everyone chuckled, focused on shovelling food into their mouths and drifted off into their own thoughts.

“Does he talk to you too, or was she just messing around?” Alice asked, apparently unwilling to be left to her thoughts.

“They have conversations. I talk to him, and he communicates telepathically by showing me images if needs be.”

“And we’re not going to talk about where she went and why she couldn’t take us with her? Or why she can teleport and we can’t?” Jen asked.

Everyone held their breaths, staring expectantly.

“No,” Agatha absently said and pressed a fry against the cheeseburger on her plate, swirling ketchup over the bun. Rio and Scratch liked to hiss at people who got too close to Agatha in particular. Possessive of her time and attention. And now they were off in their rock, probably talking about how awful Agatha was for keeping them apart.

“Why don't any of you have familiars?” Wanda thankfully drew the attention away from Agatha, who had shifted her gaze back to the rock dome.

“When I was a novice,” Lilia said, “It was believed that only the strongest witches had a familiar. A little sentient being that doesn't protect you or make you stronger. Just something exclusive, like a designer purse.”

“Is that so?” she lowly said, looking him over, attempting to gauge whether he had enough magic to stop her. She sensed nothing and he held her gaze intently, kind brown eyes making Agatha falter slightly.

“Did you know the tale of the Darkhold is a Love Story?”

Agatha snorted. The absurd claim at least took away some of the intensity. She needed to relax. Maybe it was up for sale, though only an idiot would sell something that valuable.

“Not a believer in love?”

 “She’s a lesbian,” Jen said. “She makes everything more complicated than it needs to be.”

Agatha turned to her with a raised brow. “She says as though she herself isn’t a lesbian currently in a complicated situationship.”

“Love is often complicated,” The Proprietor offered.

“Exactly,” Jen said.

“Shall I continue then?”

“Sure.” Agatha shrugged, folded her arms, and rested on her heels, focused on the display case. On the page. She needed to touch it to use it. Attune to it. Meld it with her very essence.

“During the First Cosmos, there lived a mortal witch named Chthon.”

Agatha’s gaze snapped to him. “Really? The Darkhold clearly states that Chthon was an evil male eldritch god.”

“Shh, Agatha. Let the man tell his story,” Jen piped up. “I haven’t had my daily dose of mindless entertainment to remind me that I’m not a freak and that everyone else is.”

“It’s been two days, Jen,” Agatha mumbled, despite both of them knowing that had they been home, she and Jen would’ve probably been smoking and snacking on the couch while they watched people pretending to fall in love for shit-money and two seconds of fame.

“Feels like forever,” Jen said. “Forgive my friend. Please continue.”

The Proprietor’s rich brown eyes sparkled gleefully. “Chthon lived a humble life, with dreams of protecting her family against the king’s soldiers ravaging their land. So she practised her magic every free moment she had. Which weren’t very many moments since she had a family of nine to help take care of after the kidnapping and murder of her mother.”

Jen—an only child—nodded sagely.

Agatha yawned without covering her mouth. Not because she needed to, but hoping to not be stuck there for much longer. She didn’t need a poorly made-up story to sell her on the Darkhold page, she already wanted it desperately. Maybe Rio would buy it for her. They’d been tasked to pick out something they wanted after all.

“One by one Chthon watched her family members be killed or succumb to illness because of the famine and violent oppression under the greedy king’s rule. And after she buried her six-year-old brother, and was all alone in the world, Chthon screamed to the heavens, drawing on her immense grief, and cursed the Mistress of Death for taking everything from her.”

Agatha’s gaze narrowed on him and she ignored Jen’s eyes on her.

“Lady Death, who had heard many such curses and threats, decided to show herself to Chthon, angry to be blamed when she was simply a guide to the afterlife and had nothing to do with the illnesses caused or murders perpetrated on the king’s command. Chthon refused to listen and vowed to grow stronger and one day have her vengeance on Death, for if she did not exist, her family would not have perished.”

Agatha frowned. A likely story. Rio had often mentioned how many people blamed her for their loss.  For an extremely regretful period, Agatha had been one of them.

“Death went from annoyed to amused, and spent years taunting Chthon, only fuelling her arcane studies. And as Chthon grew stronger, as Death watched her take vengeance on the king and lay waste to his armies, that amusement turned to intrigue. They went from arguing during each meeting to playfully bantering and learning each other. Missing each other in between visits. And eventually, the affection they’d cultivated into a close friendship, turned into love.”

“Aw.” Jen clasped her hands to her chest while Agatha glowered. Rio hadn’t ever mentioned Chthon, despite Agatha having the Darkhold throughout their relationship, so the story was obviously a bald-faced lie. “Did she try to kill Death at any point?” Jen asked.

The Proprietor chuckled. “Chthon had known from the start that Death is infinite and cannot be undone. They had both used her quest for vengeance as an excuse to spend time together. Both so very lonely and in need of companionship.”

Agatha sighed. “Where does the Darkhold come in?” That was the only reason she was still listening. She couldn’t care less about Lady Death/Chthon fanfiction.

The Proprietor gave her a knowing look Agatha couldn’t decipher the meaning of so she scowled at him until he continued with a smug little smile.

“Because Death is everlasting, and Chthon loved her so very much, her energies went from pretending to want to kill Death, to attempting to live forever so she may walk beside her until the end of time. Thus, ensuring that Death would never be alone again. She created a spell that could siphon magic to grow her power. It stopped her ageing. And once she had time on her side, she began crafting her dark grimoire. A tether for her soul and the magic she accumulated over millennia. To ensure it would be indestructible, and to weave a very niche selection of spells, she created her own school of magic based on the dark eldritch principles she’d mastered.”

“Chaos magic,” Agatha murmured.

“Correct. Chthon then spread copies of her grimoire across the cosmos and while she held the original in her possession, she could feed on the poor souls who neglected to heed her warnings and tried to use the borrowed power of the Darkhold for their own gain. Because you see, only Chthon can wield the eldritch magic of her grimoire without being corrupted by it. Countless tried, but their magic and sanity were siphoned into the original Darkhold and toward Chthon. In so doing, she was able to elevate herself to divinity. And thus, the God of Chaos was born.”

“So Chthon was an evil bitch,” Agatha said.

“What was evil about her?” The Proprietor tilted his head. “The Darkhold clearly states what it is and what it seeks to do. Perhaps it’s those who seek that power despite the consequences who are the “evil” ones. Many a tyrannical magic user thinking themselves above the laws of the universe has succumbed to the Book of the Damned.” He held Agatha’s stare in challenge, then added as an aside, “the terms ‘good’ and ‘evil’ are so very reductive, though. And Chthon made evil look very endearing.”

Great. The Proprietor was a fangirl.

“Where is Chthon now?” Jen asked, while Agatha questioned everything about her and Rio’s relationship. Whether she was just some watered down reminder of the woman Rio had loved billions of years ago. It couldn’t be true. Rio was many things, but she wasn’t deceptive like that. She wouldn’t pretend to love someone she didn’t.

“And herein lies their love story,” the Proprietor said through a soft smile, eyes twinkling with clear fondness. Agatha went from scowling at the floor to scowling at his disgustingly handsome face. “Only a handful of entities may survive the destruction of the cosmos. Chthon could not reach Death’s immortality, but had grown powerful enough to imbue such indestructibility on her dark grimoire. And when the First Cosmos was shattered by the Celestials, splitting it into the Multiverse and all life was destroyed along with Death’s only love—

Agatha flinched at only love.

—and the aspect Eternity was reborn and life restarted once more, Chthon’s Darkhold manifested with it. And as it was read and its pages copied and distributed, the Darkhold fed on the magic of multiple users, giving form to Chthon’s eternal soul. And eventually that soul was reborn as a baby witch.”

Jen was eating it up and Agatha felt like throwing up.

“Death, of course, could only wait patiently for this process to complete, such was demanded of the Sacred Balance. But wait she did for her Chthon to grow, to find her Darkhold, and become the woman she loved once again. The real challenge, they discovered, was Death needing to make Chthon fall in love with her all over again while she waited for Chthon’s memories to return. So you see, the Darkhold is what binds Chthon and Death together for all eternity. They have found each other in each iteration of the cosmos, and some wonder if they’re together now in the eighth.”

“You’re lying,” Agatha hoarsely said.

“What purpose do I have to lie?”

If he wasn’t a liar, it meant that Rio was. And why would Rio withhold something like that from her? Was Agatha having a copy of the Darkhold what had drawn Rio to her? Was that the basis of their entire relationship? Was it so easy for Rio to leave after Agatha asked her to because Rio knew that they’d been doomed from the start? That Chthon would eventually come to break them up?

Was Wanda Chthon reincarnated? Was that why she and Rio hit it off so quickly? They’d so easily let go of whatever feelings they had for Agatha when they were made aware of each other. The Scarlet Witch had her own bloody chapter in the Darkhold. Wanda was the most likely candidate. The only being able to wield Chthon’s chaos magic in the known universe…

Agatha grew nauseous.

“If that were true, more people would know about it,” she rasped.

“Ask her yourself then,” The Proprietor said and fucking winked.

Agatha was about to strangle him because clearly, he was pretending to know Death personally and was most likely messing with her, but she felt Wanda’s magic surge from somewhere outside. Followed by booming explosions and bloodcurdling screams.

“Shit,” she said, purple gathered around her fist and slammed it against the glass of the display case, shattering it easily. She grabbed the page and the surge of eldritch magic nearly made her knees buckle. “Sorry, I’ll come square with you if we don’t all die.”

The page was enveloped in a purple glow, orbiting Agatha as she donned her shadowy purple witch’s garb, the rush of dark magic filling her like a tease. Delicious and still not nearly enough when compared to a copy of the Darkhold.

“Agatha?” Jen said uncertainly.

“Find the others. Stay together. I’ll go find Wanda,” she said, rushing toward the screams and chaos outside.

 

Attuned to the siphoning spell, Agatha was bombarded by the magical signatures of hundreds of spellcasters throughout the village. Yet she didn’t need to search for Wanda amongst them. Even blind and miles away she would have been able to sense Wanda’s chaos magic thrumming and pulsing. Throbbing throughout the tiny hamlet as the Scarlet Witch floated up in the air above the buildings.

Agatha frowned as a few yards from the Scarlet Witch, Wanda hovered, red chaos magic nestled in the arcs of her palms.

Locking eyes with her, Agatha rose into the sky, her fingers tragically pale and her magic nowhere near Wanda’s or that of the black magic emanating from the Scarlet Witch impostor.

“Agatha!” Wanda’s voice was pure relief as she shielded against a streak of red.

The Scarlet Witch didn’t even acknowledge Agatha’s arrival.

How humiliating.

“Told you we weren’t fighting each other!” Agatha shouted back.

Wanda rolled her eyes, smothering a smile, and blasted the Scarlet Witch who waved the magic away like it was nothing.

‘You’re more powerful than her,’ Agatha telepathically said. ‘She doesn’t have chaos magic. She’s just a poor imitation.’

All technically true, but Wanda was operating at about ten per cent of her power. Unwilling to use more in fear of losing herself.

Her words did the trick though, and Wanda’s confidence grew and her attacks picked up, making the impostor actually work to defend. And with it occupied, Agatha took in the village below, swirling portals of black had sprung up. Shadow creatures flying and crawling out of them and she watched as one enveloped an unsuspecting cyborg person, its entire body turning black and wraith-like, before it immediately pounced on a cowering Traveller to do the same to them.

“Shit,” she whispered. Looking up in time to see Wanda with a translucent crown around her face.

“Are you in the mood for some double penetration, Red?”

Wanda snorted, shaking her head with a grin, but synchronised her magic with Agatha’s, blasting the fake Scarlet Witch. Agatha had hoped to gain her attention, but she waved off her magic and focused on Wanda, as though she knew what retaliation against Agatha would mean.

She couldn’t even be relieved that this was most likely what Lilia had seen in her vision. Not when the screams were still echoing from below. Agatha was only keeping it together because she could feel the coven’s vibrant magic amongst the hoard of Travellers.

‘Let me know how we're doing, ladies,’ Agatha said through their link.

‘On the roof with Lilia. Yellow building. Jen shielding. I'm blasting.’

Agatha spotted them on a flat rooftop a hundred yards away, Rio standing with them, brows knitted as her eyes flickered over the portals. Having her with the coven made Agatha feel more at ease and she gathered her magic to focus back on the impostor. But then darkness fell, as though night had sneaked up on them.

Staring into the sky, Agatha’s stomach dropped and she froze at the gigantic person-shaped silhouette that loomed in the sky, body littered with burning stars, shadowed horns protruding from a featureless face. The air crackled with its raw power.

“Nothing can help you now,” the shadow’s smooth voice rolled over them, clear and crisp despite the screams sounding from below. “Your own systems have been corrupted. Turned against you. They will devour you from the inside out.” At the mountain peaks, a shield rose as though trying to form a dome around the entire valley. “And I will absorb what scraps are left of you, Eternity.” Agatha’s head snapped toward the rooftop where the tiger cubs had scampered beneath Rio’s robes, little scorpion tales sticking out. “And all will be as it was, long ago. Before your foul kind. Before the Multiverses. Eighth and Seventh...and Sixth...and Fifth...and back and back...dying and being born, over and over. Like filthy little organisms.”

Rio lifted her hands, long fingers curled and Agatha realised she was the one casting the shield, which had risen about halfway to closing over the village. She’d seen Rio put up shields instantaneously, the effort going into this one meant that the entity in the sky required that much to be deterred.

“We will return to a saner time,” it continued, drawing Agatha’s attention again, while Wanda continued to fight her evil twin. “When there was but one cosmos. One universe. One reality. One totality. When there was only I. The First Firmament. And soon...I will be the last.”

It lifted one of its gigantic arms, a shadowy spear appearing in its grip, and tossed it downward. The spear travelled like a bullet, fast on the release and growing smaller on its trajectory. Its other arm raised instantly, six times in rapid succession, six shadow spears leaving its grip before Rio’s shield closed and the First Firmament chuckled deeply, and dissipated, leaving behind a pale pink sky.

Agatha looked back to the rooftop and the world stopped.

Rio stood, blood seeping from her mouth and nose, four of the spears impaled in her chest, piercing out of her back. Jen and Alice held her upright while Lilia sheltered the Twins in her arms.

“No…” Agatha whispered, heart thundering in her ears, hand going to clutch at the locket around her neck.

Rio eyes fluttered closed, her body falling limp, Jen and Alice gently lowered with her. The spears faded and the cubs scrambled out of Lilia’s arms and ran to Rio, nudging at her lifeless body.

All Agatha could think was how much Nicky had looked like Rio and how Rio now looked like he had that morning.

Her magic crackled, a searing heat spread up her chest and neck. She was vaguely aware of the First Firmament’s shadows wreaking havoc across the hamlet, closing in on the building and the Twins, as though that had been their destination all along. They crawled up the walls and Alice rose from Rio’s side to continue blasting the wraiths that came flying toward them, closing in on the coven in a dark skittering wave.

Agatha called on the magic around her. Her hands elegantly shaped an almost familiar pattern, her lips moved in a whispered incantation. Purple strands of magic pulled taut between her fingers as she connected to all the magic users in the village. Her magic hooked onto their essences like fish at the end of a line. Eyes falling shut, overwhelmed at the multitude of sensations, she raised her arms in the air and reeled the magic toward her body.

The weaker Travellers fell instantly, Agatha trembling at the familiar and welcome rush of being filled. The black magic of the wraiths and crawlers followed, and she opened her eyes to watch as the wave of shadows ascending on the coven turned to ash that drifted away on the breeze. She moaned lewdly when the magic of the more powerful casters filled her, breathed in deeply when the coven’s magic joined theirs, and shuddered when Wanda’s chaos magic poured into her veins.

Her head lolled back and she cackled madly, tingling with a arousal, a rainbow of hundreds of magic streams entering her from across the hamlet, filling her to the brim and making her feel invincible. Her eyes flashed, glowing with power, and when Rio’s still body came into focus, Agatha screamed, spun around, and blasted purple lightning into the Scarlet Witch’s chest. A constant stream of pure concentrated magic entered the impostor and Agatha used its body as a conduit to chain the lighting toward the portals, destroying them and whatever had still been trying to crawl out.

It was exhilarating, devastating, as the magic nearly exploded out of her, her body unused to holding so much. The impostor was evaporated, along with every magical being in the hamlet…

Agatha hovered in the sky, chest heaving, and ears buzzing at the sudden deafening quiet.

A a jolt of panic, regret, and grief shocked her into action as she wildly turned to the rooftop and nearly fell from the sky in relief when she spotted the coven, weakened but alive. Wanda had joined them at some point. All of them looked as though they’d spent days crawling the desert without food and water. Pale and worried, but standing and not desiccated corpses.

Shaking with adrenaline, Agatha flew down to where Rio lay. Lilia and Alice held a whimpering tiger cub each and Jen was trying in vain to heal Rio’s chest where the spears had faded, and left behind black scorching burn marks.

And Rio…

Agatha fell to her knees and gently lifted Rio’s limp body into her arms, brushing her lips against a cool pale forehead.

“Darling?” Agatha croaked, brushing the hair from Rio’s face, unable to think clearly enough to know what to do. Her ouroboros were glowing brightly and she looked toward Rio’s disturbingly bare wrists.

An ache punctured her heart, so painful, she whimpered in agony.

“Apologies, Agatha's Coven,” Rio’s disembodied voice sounded from all around them and Agatha’s body unspooled with a relieved sob, shoulders shaking as tears ran down her cheeks. “It appears that birthing the Twins has drawn the attention of the First Firmament. I’ve opened a portal, if you could please enter and make your way to safety.”

No one moved, and Agatha was unable to, furiously trembling in relief.

“Agatha? Sweetheart?” Rio’s omnipresent voice gently caressed over her. “I’ll fix my body once I’ve taken care of a few things.”

Agatha sniffed and rose to her feet, lifting Rio’s body with her, unable to let go.

She scanned the hamlet, avoided looking at the coven, and instantly spotted the portal. It wasn’t a Gate, wobbling in a more circular shape, a black abyss centred instead of the glittering white they’d gotten used to. Agatha held Rio close, the adrenaline wearing off, the guilt that she’d taken the coven’s magic slowly rising. She hadn’t known she could siphon magic that way and had nearly killed them all in the process. That replayed in her mind and she didn’t have enough left in her to think about the appearance of the First Firmament and how powerful it was. How quickly its army had multiplied, and what it aimed to do to the cosmos. Didn’t want to think about how Wanda was Rio’s long-lost love reincarnate, and what to do with that information.

The Darkhold had never showed her the chaos magic spells. Only the dark magic that made her broody and intense. Like it was reserving those spells for someone else. For Wanda. And what would she do when Rio realised? She had to know who Wanda was already. What would Wanda do? What would Rio do? Would she lose them both? Would she fight for another chance with Rio? Should she? Was it fair? Had it been anyone other than Wanda... Wanda who stood back and didn’t complicate an already complicated situation to give Agatha a chance at happiness…

She shut the chaotic string of thought down and quietly followed the coven, only looking away once from Rio’s face and marred chest, to make sure that the cubs were with Lilia and Alice.

“I didn't even get to buy anything,” Jen grumpily mumbled as Agatha carefully carried Rio's body through the portal.

 

Chapter 9: The Realm of Death

They stepped into the entry hall of a mansion. Gothic chic, with elaborate candelabras of varying sizes hanging from a high ceiling and abstract greyscale paintings decorating dark stone walls.

On hearing Jen’s shriek, Agatha looked up from Rio's face and saw a skeleton standing in front of them wearing a red bow tie. Her lips twitched. Rio was hilarious. And then she looked back down—instinctively wanting to share in the joke—and all amusement left her.

“I am Bartol Utler,” the skeleton said in a ridiculously posh English accent. “Mistress has instructed me to escort you to the guest wing where you may rest. She will join you later.”

“It speaks,” Alice excitedly whispered. Surprised as though they hadn’t walked through a squadron of Rio’s Legion of the Doomed. Granted, none of those Undead had spoken to them and the coven had mistaken them for demons.

Bartol held out his bony arms as though waiting to receive Rio, and Agatha instinctively pulled her tighter against her chest, cradling her in a protective layer of magic. He simply lowered his arms and inclined his head, motioning with scraggy fingers toward a set of stained-glass doors—the only doors in the entry hall after the portal disappeared—before turning in that direction.

They followed him into the aforementioned guest wing, entering a lavish hallway that looked like a five-star hotel. Bartol walked into the first bedroom on the left, which was neat and decorated in a minimalist fashion, and that was all Agatha registered before she gently lay Rio on the queen-sized bed, sat down beside her and took hold of her too cold hand.

The First Firmament had the power to effortlessly pierce Rio’s mortal vessel. Agatha hadn’t ever seen Rio injured that way before, or so still and empty. She touched her fingers to Rio’s cool cheek, the way she’d touched Nicky. Even at six years old he’d been the spitting image of Rio.

Her breath caught, her chest tightened, and she pulled trembling fingers back to her lap continuing to clutch Rio’s hand, needing Rio to get back into her body before she lost her mind entirely.

The tiger cubs were placed on the bed, but as if they knew Rio wasn’t there, they darted to Agatha instead.

Rio was fine. She was certain of it, and still Agatha couldn’t leave her side.

“Bart, why don’t you show your mistress’s guests to where they’ll be staying,” she murmured. “I’ll remain with her vessel.”

“Of course, my lady,” he said and walked off.

Agatha felt Wanda’s hand on her shoulder and stiffened. Chaos magic trickled down her spine at the gentle squeeze that followed. She shuddered at the touch, relieved at how brief it was. Fighting down the surge of her own magic readying to attack.

She hadn’t been able to look at any of their gaunt features. Sick at the thought of what she’d done, nauseous at the idea of Chthon’s connection to Rio.

When the room was quiet, she settled beside Rio, curled up against her side, arm slung across her stomach, absently letting the cubs play with her hand. Exhausted from all that power entering and leaving her body, Agatha soon drifted off to sleep.

#

She woke to an empty bed and an empty room. No Twins and no one else.

Laying on her back, she contemplated which emotional crisis to go deal with first. And unwilling to face Rio just yet, she got up with a sigh, walked into the hallway, and instantly heard the rowdy coven from somewhere down the corridor.

They were laughing and talking as though they hadn’t been attacked by a cosmic entity out to destroy literally everything, just a few hours ago. Like they didn’t have their magic stolen by someone they had trusted. There were only four of them, yet they always made every room feel full and alive.

She neared the area they were in, slowing her gait and walked through the doorway, wringing her hands and dragging her feet across the tiles. Stopping when a large Turkish style bath house came into view. Bright yellow walls and opulent gold furbishing greeted her. A domed ceiling was painted like a blue sky, brightening the multitudes of greenery spread across the space to create a lush oasis surrounding an Olympic sized pool.

Rio loved water. Loved swimming. She would go diving in the ocean and spend hours down there exploring. Agatha wasn’t a fan, and had usually waited for her reading on the shore or floating on a boat. Bath houses and bathtubs though, she’d always joined Rio in those.

Before she could get lost in the pleasant memories, Agatha’s gaze landed on the coven who thankfully appeared physically recovered. They hadn’t noticed her hovering as they lounged on comfy chairs instead of being in the water. Bartol Utler was there too, serving wine and snacks and Agatha wanted to smile at their smiles, but her stomach twisted and she took a few steps into view, standing at the pool’s edge opposite to where they were seated across the expanse of crystal-clear water.

“Agatha!” Jen grinned. “How’s Rio’s body doing?”

Her heart clenched at the genuine query. Rio had made such a big impression on all of them in such a short time.

“Uh, fine. She’ll be fine.”

“We can ask for literally anything and Bartol brings it!” Alice said, holding up a garish diamond encrusted Patek Phillipe watch on her wrist.

Agatha licked her lips and ran a shaky hand through her hair. “Uhm…”

They frowned, smiles falling from their faces, worriedly looking at her.

“Agatha?” Wanda asked.

From the plants on either side of Agatha, two red imps came flying toward her body. Agatha remarkably recognised them and caught the Twins in her arms. They nuzzled into her neck and she held them to her chest, careful of their bat-like wings, her shoulders loosening as she inhaled the subtle scent of woodfire and petrichor.

The coven looked on in a mixture of awe and amusement.

“I wanted to apologise,” Agatha mumbled, rubbing her chin against Infinity’s smooth bald head. “For siphoning your magic.”

“Oh,” Alice said. “That’s okay.”

“Yeah.” Jen shrugged.

Lilia and Wanda nodded.

Agatha frowned. “What?”

“No need to apologise,” Jen said. “Desperate times and all that.”

“Desperate times…” Agatha said, dumbfounded. “I killed a few hundred people…and other things.”

“Unfortunate for them,” Lilia said. “But you didn’t kill us.”

Everyone nodded and Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Seriously?”

“Yes,” Jen said. “Next time, definitely ask, but we understand that those were extenuating circumstances. With monsters everywhere, Rio getting speared with shadowy magic, Wanda fighting her evil doppelganger, the cosmic entity who wants to destroy everything appearing in the sky, and all that.”

“I nearly passed out,” Alice mumbled. Lilia nodded along, nibbling a piece of mango, looking disturbed.

“You saved us,” Wanda said, smiling broadly, eyes crinkling with affection.

“Could you always do that?” Lilia asked. “I thought you were only able to take magic when attacked.”

Agatha was great at adjusting spells, but to do so required research and time. Siphoning in that manner, the instinctive way she’d known the incantation and hand gestures to pull the magic toward her…It had to have been the page that was different. She would need to study it more closely later.

Agatha cleared her throat. “No. That was new. I didn’t know I could do it either.”

“It certainly did the trick,” Wanda said. “Those shadows were closing in on the coven.”

Agatha stared at the water, unable to comprehend why they didn’t hate her. She’d done far less and had been met with scorn and judgement.

“Agatha.” Lilia stared at her with that unsettling matriarchal look she got from time to time. “Do you know why we didn’t lose our minds when we arrived in the Outside?”

“Because you didn’t understand enough to lose your minds?”

“Because you assured us that we would be safe with Rio. And do you know why we accepted that Rio would lead us out?”

“No?”

“Because you were the one telling us to accept it.”

“You don’t ever listen to me. You argue with me all the time. You questioned me about Rio repeatedly.”

“We listen when it matters,” Lilia said. “Though we also enjoy riling you up.” All of them cackled merrily and Agatha rolled her eyes. Lilia continued. “We aren’t lonely or scared and struggling anymore, because you brought us together. We finally feel powerful because you are in this coven with us. You make us feel safe to be who we are, and that, my dear friend, is something none of us had experienced in a very long time.”

Agatha’s neck and cheeks burned and she awkwardly shifted in place. “Shut up,” she said, swallowing down the knot in her throat, glancing away from Wanda softly staring at her. “Don’t be disgusting,” she muttered. But walked closer to them, gently holding the imps who were dozing on her shoulders, warmth filling her for everyone in that room.

How humiliating.

She went to sit in the chair diagonally from Jen and Wanda on a two-seater. Wanda stared at the imp Twins like Agatha had seen her staring at babies. Like she wanted to abduct them from their mothers and raise them as her own.

A twinge of empathy caused by the knowledge of Wanda’s loss had Agatha offering Eternity to her, his blue eyes drowsy with sleepiness, a tiny red thumb in his mouth. Wanda took him so very carefully and sat back, revealing Jen with outstretched arms. Agatha sighed and handed Infinity to her.

Feeling empty and exposed, she summoned Scratchy onto her lap causing Jen and Wanda to slowly shift further away.

Lilia snorted. “Bunch of brooding hens.”

Alice stared at Jen, lips parted and eyes rounded in wonderment, before she shook her head and cleared her throat. “So, what was your judgement about, Lilia? We never got a chance to ask.”

“I was wrong about my biggest fear,” Lilia said, eyes growing distant. “I thought it was death. Everyone I cared about died. The people I tried to warn with my visions all died. It felt like a curse, as though Death was chasing me...Rio helped me understand that Death doesn't come for people, she simply waits for them to come to her.”

Agatha hummed softly, petting Scratchy, whilst staring at the Twins.

“It was enough for the city that I finally accepted that it wasn't my responsibility to save those who died not heeding my warnings. That sometimes, people died simply because it was their time.”

Everyone fell silent, having all suffered loss. Having had blamed Death themselves, and fought to change the outcome. Agatha hadn’t realised that Lilia carried that fear with her. Though understood now why she’d been such a recluse when Agatha had found her and had to harass her into joining the coven.

“Okay…” Jen said when the melancholy silence stretched for far too long. “Speaking of Rio…”

Agatha stiffened.

“Yeah,” Alice agreed. “Glad she’s safe and all but are we going to need to go beat her up for the Chthon thing?”

“Of course Jen told you.”

“Why wouldn’t I? Personally, I think it’s just a made-up story. But there was something weird about that guy at the shop.”

Agatha certainly agreed with the part about The Proprietor.

“Having a whole secret soulmate and not telling you doesn’t seem like something she would do given how she is about you,” Wanda said.

Heat burned in Agatha’s belly, her hackles rising. “You’ve known her for all of five seconds.”

“Fair enough. Do you think it’s something she would do?”

Agatha fought down the irrational part of her that wanted to lash out, jaw tight with the effort. “The only truth we know is that Chthon created chaos magic and there’s only one being in the known universe who has it.”

She glared at Wanda who at first looked confused and then it dawned on her and her lips parted. “You can’t seriously think I’m Chthon, Agatha,” she harshly whispered.

Jen gasped at the revelation.

“You wouldn’t know it if you were.”

“It’s a stupid story. Rio’s clearly crazy about you.”

“Because Chthon,” she pointed accusingly at Wanda, purple sparking in her hand, “hasn’t remembered yet.”

“No,” Wanda said, looking perturbed as she cradled Eternity to her and got up as though she wanted to get away from Agatha. “Get that out of your head right now before you self-sabotage all of the progress you’ve made.”

Agatha averted her gaze, shoulders stiff, and petted Scratch, who for once didn’t fight her smothering him with desperate affection.

“Wanda’s right,” Lilia carefully said. “Go ask Rio instead of us sitting here speculating over gossip. We’ll look after the kids.”

“It could just be the First Firmament messing with you to try and fuck with Rio,” Jen said.

“The First Firmament also created a copy of the Scarlet Witch and not me,” Agatha muttered, but rose from her seat and placed Scratch down onto it to keep an eye on the Twins. She then walked out of the bath house not because she wanted to go clarify anything, but needing to go give Rio a piece of her mind.

“Agatha don’t leave us alone with your demon rabbit!” Jen loudly hissed after her.

 

Agatha had always wondered why Rio had chosen her. They’d met when she was a young adult who’d just killed her mother and coven and was slowly falling off the deep-end. Why else would someone like Rio have taken an interest in her? It certainly wasn’t because of her sparkling personality. She’d been remarkable only because of the copy of the Darkhold she’d held.

 Grateful for the siphoning page, she donned her witch’s garb like armour, draping herself in the shadowy shades of purple that made her feel powerful. Puffing up and growing her hair in a way she knew would leave Rio weak.

The elegant foyer of Death’s Dark Palace contained only the glass door to the guest wing. And the guest wing only held their rooms, the bath house, a dining room, and a lounge and bar leading out onto a gorgeous terrace overlooking a pitch-black lake.

Scowling, Agatha used her ouroboros to sense Rio, contemplating teleporting to her, but wanted Rio to feel her coming.

A grey door appeared in front of her.

Agatha clenched a fist and opened the door with her other hand. It led into a wine-red hallway lined with framed photographs of landscapes from alien planets. Some bright and colourful, others monochromatic, depicting various biomes beneath large moons and suns, burning stars and bright constellations.

Refusing to get distracted by the stunning pictures, she marched down the corridor to the green door that appeared at the end, entering a massive hall that looked like a cathedral. Or rather, a museum as there were various displays containing large statues featuring different species of alien races dressed in foreign regalia. Below each statue were smaller displays of bladed weapons and instruments. Some held futuristic gadgets and trinkets, others were more primitive containing stone tablets and carved ornaments.

It was mesmerising. The room appeared to stretch endlessly, and Agatha was enraptured as she walked toward a harp-like string instrument, three times her size at the foot of a statue of an amphibian-like being.

She ran a finger across the strings, closing her eyes at the soothing acoustics that filtered around the room while she experimentally plucked in search of familiar keys… Then she froze. Her eyes flashed open and she growled under her breath because Rio had led her there to calm her down. To distract her from her anger.

She pushed her annoyance through her ouroboros and went in search of a door that appeared a moment later right in front of her. Her anger reignited at the audacity, that Rio’s plan had nearly worked, and flipped her hair, clenched her jaw, and reached for the handle.

The second she touched it, Agatha felt a tug in her stomach then found herself standing in a beautiful greenhouse, outside a set of charcoal double doors made of embossed and hammered iron, decorated with Neo-Renaissance motifs, Rio’s presence calling to her from the other side.

Growing angrier that she’d been summoned, Agatha magically flung the doors open and marched into a sleek modern bedroom. One wall was made entirely of glass and a large full moon shone above a dark forest and rolling grey hilltops, bathing the interior in a silvery glow.

Across the entryway, a king-sized bed was decorated with dark sheets and covers and above the black slat headboard, against a blue-grey wall, another landscape photograph spread the width of it. A burning red sunset over a shadowy world, brilliant purple lava flowing through cracks in a black mountainous region.

In one corner a dark side-table held a pale clay pot filled with soil containing silver-white roses that bloomed and sparkled beneath the moonlight.

She turned, took a sip of her drink, and leaned her hip against the backrest of a white recliner, no doubt placed there to stare out at the beauty of the endless night in the Realm of Death.

Agatha’s gaze fell to the smooth unmarred skin on Rio’s chest where the spears had pierced and burned her, then travelled down to make sure that the ouroboros tattoos were indeed back where they belonged. They glowed a pretty purple and moved under Agatha’s attention.

“Yes.”

She remembered asking Rio about past lovers. Rio had said that Agatha was the first mortal she’d been with.

Liar.

Or was she simply playing with the truth since Chthon was technically a god and not a mortal…

Agatha’s eyes watered with hurt she struggled to push down, and she tried to keep hold of her anger instead. “Why do you need a bed when you don’t sleep?”

“Sometimes I enjoy laying down when I masturbate thinking of you.”

Agatha bit the inside of her cheek—forcing away the image of Rio on that bed with her legs spread apart and her hand working between her thighs—simply refusing to be horny. Not when Rio’s betrayal was still lodged in her chest, making it painful to breathe.

“You’re into photography, now?” she asked, finally recognising how similar in style the photographs were to the beautiful paintings in the villa.

“Always have been.”

“And just decided not to tell me? What else have you been hiding?”

“I could hardly show you my camera from another world and another time in the 1700s, Agatha.”

Agatha breathed through her nose, needing to be angry and not sad. Rio was a liar. Rio had made her feel like shit for supposedly cheating whilst hiding an entire soulmate from her.

Had learned them and studied them for decades because Rio had been her world. Her everything. And she didn’t need to confirm it, Chthon meant something to Rio. “What do you think you know, Agatha?”

“Because there are only a handful of people in the entire cosmos who would tell that story.”

“So it’s true.”

“Some guy at a magic shop.”

“Some guy?”

“Yes, some guy, which doesn’t matter. Is it true?”

Rio locked their eyes defiantly. “Yes.”

Rio shook her head and walked closer, pretty, brown eyes glimmering. “Agatha…” she murmured, and took hold of Agatha’s waist, making her squirm.

“Don’t look at me like that,” Agatha croaked, feeling weak and needing Rio close. Wanting to tell her to fuck off. Needing it to be a lie. She blinked rapidly, trying to stop the sting of tears in her eyes.

“I figured it out. Wanda’s Chthon.”

“You are Chthon.”

“Rio, don’t fuck with me right now.”

“I dunno, payback for the emotional torture I put you through?”

“You wouldn’t deserve it.”

She’d suspected Wanda yes, but mostly she’d gone there for Rio to tell her that it was fiction. A lie. That Chthon was what the Darkhold said and the Death fandom was just pairing Rio up with random powerful beings.

Your soul doesn’t wander about upsetting the Sacred Balance. The Wanda thing would be you hijacking bodies. Cheating death. Cheating me. Always a cheater.”

Attempted to process the absurd things coming out of Rio’s mouth. Rio had never treated her like she was naive or dumb, so to expect her to just believe something so unbelievable…There had to be a catch. Something she was missing.

“Where are we going?”

“You asked me to bring you here after I told you who you are.”

What an absolutely insane sentence to hear.

“Okay,” Agatha said, and stalked through the door and into a blinding white room. Large tiled floors and walls, even the ceiling was sectioned into blocks. A perfect empty cube that looked about thirty by thirty feet with a red tiled square in the centre providing the only alternate colour.

She suppressed a smile that Rio had been sipping apple juice from her wetbar like it was a fine cognac—unsurprising, yet still so endearing—and tried not to stare at the way her long dark lashes lay atop her cheeks.

She was supposed to be angry.

“Not sure.”

“Nope.”

“No, you didn’t tell me.”

“Don’t turn this into something vile.”

As you may have noticed, too many cosmic entities are either nihilistic or power hungry. Or a deadly combination of both. Constantly fighting over control like toddlers with a toy they eventually break with their greed and entitlement.”

Agatha pressed her fingers into her hair, wanting to pull it out by the roots. “This is insane, Rio.”

“Which is why I never tell you and wait for you to start poking around for answers. It’s always easier to let you figure it out yourself. You created the Darkhold to guide you through that process.”

“And these?” She held up her wrists. “They’re obviously different to the usual hand-fasting tattoos. Do they have something to do with Chthon?”

“My creator married us during the First Cosmos, so they’re pretty permanent. Eternity just allowed you to see them when we got married this time round. They are hand-fasting tattoos. A symbol of our love and commitment.”

Agatha wasn’t sure what she felt other than disbelief and suspicion. And ridiculous because she knew Rio wouldn’t lie about something like this. She wouldn’t be so cruel…

“Do I look the same?”

“Yes. Which is why I’ve come to favour this form.” Rio motioned to her own face and then softly smiled. “You have this way of looking at me I can’t wait to see again in each iteration.”

“Do you remember when we visited Hierve el Agua? You'd just turned five and twenty.”

“Still a virgin nerd by the way, no thanks to you.”

Rio grinned, her eyes crinkling and Agatha's heart soared at the look and the memory.

“You’ve always loved the mountains.”

Agatha hummed, having longed for them throughout the day.

“That was the first time you looked at me like that again. Your eyes were the colour of the sky and it felt like I finally got you back...” Rio’s smile fell away, and she grew taut, then cleared her throat. “Anyway,” she said motioning to the red square, but Agatha remained rooted in place. Watching her.

She remembered that day clearly. Remembered feeling so confident that she would love Rio forever. Come what may. She'd most likely stopped looking at Rio ‘that way’ after Nicky died. When she’d buried her heart with him and the world had faded to nothing. When she’d felt only pain and rage, unable to recognise anything good that still existed around her.

Rio smiled sadly. “Nicky was…a miracle, our only one. We’ve spoken about it. We revisit it often. We conclude each time that no parent should outlive their child. We worry of the enemies that might use them against us. Might hurt them because of us… It’s always been a tough conversation to have.”

I wish you would remember.

The words Rio had spoken in the City of Judgement hit Agatha like a freight train. Whispered with such anguish that Agatha had no choice but to believe. Her heart skipped and thudded against her chest and in her brain.

“If this is true, Rio, why couldn’t Nicky also—

You of course were too stubborn to fail. What you accomplished, I doubt it can ever be replicated. “What? You’re not staying?”

“You asked me not to.”

“And you just do whatever she says, even if I might be in danger?”

The room was creepy, far too white and bright. The red square felt sinister. Like a bullseye target.

“When it comes to this, you decide what’s best for you. I don’t interfere.”

Agatha scoffed. “Tell the coven not to cremate my body. I want to be embalmed and immortalised in a pyramid.”

And then she just left. Abandoned Agatha in an asylum cell. How apt.

But, the moment the door vanished, the room began to change. A plush carpet shimmered into existence around the infernal red square. Floor to ceiling bookshelves appeared along the walls to her sides packed with tomes. A fireplace with roaring purple flames was ahead, nestled between two large windows revealing the familiar moonlit backdrop of the Realm of Death.

Fiddleleaf fig plants, ferns, monstera and evergreens hung in pots from the windows and ceiling, some familiar, some alien. Succulents were potted and spaced in designer compartments between the bookshelves, and planted in tall ceramic urns tastefully scattered around the room. In one corner, the Darkhold lay on an obsidian pedestal. Shadowy purple flames licked across the cover, violet embers glowed along the page edges. Agatha could tell it was the original simply from the sheer size of the tome. Despite it not being centred, it still called attention to itself. She could practically hear the whispers in her head…

A black winged back chair materialised directly in front of her, and Agatha’s lips parted at the woman seated on it. Legs crossed at the knee, wearing a pair of tall heeled boots with a black tailored suit, violet material peaking from crisp cuffs and below a sharp mandarin collar. “Please resist the urge to move from the red square. Having to replay my theatrical reveal will ruin the entire effect.”

My wife and my children.

The words replayed in Agatha's brain. The possessiveness, the confidence, and certainty in which Rio had proclaimed them. Agatha had loved hearing it, loved Rio’s righteous anger at Fury daring to blame her for the end of the cosmos. Hated that despite all that, Rio felt as far away from her as she'd been since they were reunited. Continuing to claim her out loud without making any moves to actually do so.

Rio wore no shirt beneath her fitted jacket held together by a singular brave button. Chapter 12: The Junction To Everywhere

After appearing in the empty throne room of the Dark Fortress, Agatha pondered her next step. She’d left on a whim, acting on impulse, and was now back to doubting her choice as she considered that Rio might have left the party to get some time away from her.

“Fancy meeting you here,” Rio said from beside her and Agatha released a breath through a relieved smile.

To prevent any further damage to the cosmic balance, I needed to recreate the Twins while The First Firmament was still in the area and placed them in that shield while I was held up fighting off its shadow army. It found them, couldn’t break through the shield, so sent them to your Earth as a threat.”

Chthon leapt out of the portal, landing in the silver blades of grass, and rolled a few times to extinguish the green flames burning through her witch’s robes.

She tossed and turned and finally settled breathlessly on her back, her satchel beside her and groaned at the feather-light weight of Scratchy appearing on her chest.

‘Shut up.’
