‘Do you want to do the rest alone?’

‘Yes, please.’

She chuckled as his whiskers tickled her neck in a goodbye nuzzle before he vanished, no doubt to go harass Bart.

Jumping to her feet, Chthon brushed off the dust from her scorched clothes, rolled her eyes at herself, and repaired the damage with a flick of her wrist. After retrieving her satchel and placing it over her shoulder, she set her sights on the obsidian pyramid about a mile away.

 

She entered what some on Earth might describe as the Garden of Eden. The glass inside the pyramid reflected a clear blue sky, sun rays breaking through the thick green foliage. Trees and plants decorated the inside, sectioned by pretty stone pathways that ran throughout the large surface area and was lined with colourful flower beds.

Chthon walked toward the centre where a small waterfall cascaded into a pretty pond covered in water lilies and lotus flowers. The trees gave way to a grass covered meadow where the only notable structures were the seven sarcophagi propped up to face the gorgeous water fixture at a forty-five degree angle.

Each sarcophagus was made of its own unique material, wood-crafted, metal-crafted, and stone-crafted. Yet what bound them by design, was River’s signature style and artistry. The time and care that had gone into creating a final resting place for her bodies, always brought a bittersweet smile to Chthon’s face.

River knew they were only vessels. Knew they would see each other again one day. And yet she’d built this memorial inside her heart. Somewhere she visited frequently, especially when Chthon was absent.

She swallowed thickly.

What was once River’s special place, had now become theirs. River shared it openly and freely and Chthon doubted there was anything in the cosmos River wouldn’t give her should she want it.

Her chest tightened, eyes landing on the eighth sarcophagi. A smaller one nearest to the waterfall in its own special place. Behind it, River had crafted shelving in the shape of a tree. On the branched platforms, she’d placed small whittled animals. Like the ones she’d gifted Nicky on his birthday each year.

There were well over two hundred of them, Chthon had memorised them all. Hadn’t dared touch any, yet she still recognised the newest one that had been added. A tiny platypus. Which meant River had already been there that day.

She lowered onto the lush grass at the foot of the small sarcophagus and opened up her satchel.

Chthon was careful to not leave anything behind after her visits. Not in there. River had said she could, but it was enough for her that both of them could finally have this. That they were able to stand beside each other and mourn their son. Especially on days like today when every thought became ‘what if’…

“It’s a Blood Moon, which means your mother’s going to go all out again,” she murmured as she watched her careful spellwork mould the items to her will. “But I won’t let her win this time.” She chuckled to herself.

Wanda’s therapist had said that even if Nicky couldn’t hear her, it was still good for Chthon to express the things she wanted him to know out loud. To not keep them inside.

She sighed, that familiar doubt creeping up her belly. Two years since her core memories had returned. Two years since grasping the full extent of her immortality. She was still only at sixty percent of her power. But two years of knowing and she couldn’t shake this one persistent thought…

“Do you think that this time I should come to you?” She finally gave voice to it. The guilt. The longing. The feeling of her utter failure as a mother…

Tears burned in her eyes, falling onto the burning green embers she was carefully crafting.

All Chthon had ever had, had ever wanted and needed, was River. Now Nicky was there in the Spirit Realm. Joining him meant leaving River. Continuing this cycle of rebirth meant being unable to see Nicky again.

Her intent had been immortality. She wasn’t sure the magic could even be reversed. The only way she could think of would be if the indestructible Darkhold could be destroyed. If Scratchy was destroyed… Her soul was intrinsically linked to him. They were bound as tightly and irrevocably as she and River was. Chthon’s life felt like theirs as much as it was her own.

She touched the handle, the flowers bursting into pretty green flames and River looked ready to explode as she stared at it with wide eyes filled with want.

“Their fire burns as eternal as my love for you,” Chthon said and smirked at the predictable groans that followed, loving every second of the coven’s discomfort and River’s delight, who poked her tongue into her cheek, gaze dragging lazily from the broom to Chthon, who could tell that River intended to express her gratitude for the gift very thoroughly.

She licked her lips when River held out her fists, pressed them side-by-side, and then slowly moved them apart, a broom taking shape in the space widening in front of her.

With a gasp, Chthon took in the dark midnight handle, glittering with tiny stars and constellations. The head was like the nucleus of a comet, a violet dust trail bursting out to form a gorgeous tail.

“This is an undiscovered quasar galaxy,” River murmured, staring at Chthon, while Chthon stared at the broom. “Uninhabited by sentient life since its formation five billion years ago. It's most extraordinary feature is its sun, that radiates a luminescent glow reminiscent of your eyes.” Rio’s fingers trailed across the top of the broomhead where the purple sun seemed to be encased in glass, likely lending the dust trail its brilliant violet hue. “I gift you this galaxy to be viewed and enjoyed for the ten million years it will take its black hole to swallow it entirely. I hope that each time you look at it, you’ll be reminded of how utterly its beauty pales in comparison to yours.”

Chthon grinned widely at the groans from the coven, matching River’s brilliant smile.

Alice and Jen actually facepalmed and Chthon gleefully ignored them as she rushed toward River who met her halfway and crashed their mouths together.

“I love it,” she mumbled, in between kisses, wrestling River to the ground who willingly went down, letting herself be pinned.

“I love you,” River said, bucking up into her.

“I hate you both so much,” Jen muttered.

Alice sighed. “You’re lucky this place is the best vacation spot, or we would ignore all your calls.”

“Should we just come back later?” Wanda asked.

River smiled and their teeth knocked when Chthon smiled too. But she got up and helped River off the ground.

One of their favourite things these days, was making the coven cringe, who after watching far too many cosmic monologues and intense farewell declarations of eternal love, assumed that—“because they were old as time”—it was just the ridiculous way they spoke to each other on occasion.

“No, I want to test out my new broom,” Chthon said. Summoning Rio’s gift closer, who did the same with her pretty galaxy broom so they could exchange them.

“Thank god,” Jen muttered and they all paired up again.

River’s hand brushed against hers, a silent promise as she carefully took her gift.

They touched their broomheads together. Their ouroboros lighting up as their magic mingled. As River allowed a taste of her own power to flow through the coven connection. Soothing, calming, slotting perfectly in place like a puzzle piece.

Chthon stared softly into pretty brown eyes. Unadulterated happiness filling her chest to bursting capacity.

“Pro te, dilecta, aperio viam,” they murmured in perfect harmony, the echoes of the coven accentuating the declaration.

For you, beloved, I open the way.

*********

THE END
